If this works then the problem is with DNS.
You have to specify DNS servers in /etc/resolv.conf

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Sep  1 20:46:05 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Sep  1 20:44:27 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (OGGDEC)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509012033020.20952-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

RUTE User's Tutorial and Exposition, One of best free book for 
GNU/Linux. URL: http://web.whittier.edu/jlutgen/rute/rute.html

One Day One Command 
===================

oggdec -- Decodes Ogg into PCM Audio format.

Summary:

Ogg Vorbis is a new audio compression format. It is different from
these other formats because it is completely free, open & unpatented.
It is roughly comparable to other formats used to store & play digital
music, such as MP3, VQF, AAC, and other digital audio formats.

oggdec decodes Ogg Vorbis files into PCM-encoded ("uncompressed")  
audio files, either WAV or RAW format.  For each input file, oggdec
writes to a filename based on the input filename, but with the extn
changed to ".wav" or ".raw".


Examples:

$ locate .ogg -- Search for some OGG files in your system.

$ oggdec in.ogg -- Decode in.ogg and writes to in.wav file.

$ oggdec --raw=1 in.ogg -- Decode in.ogg and writes to in.raw file.

$ oggdec in.ogg -o out.wav -- Decode in.ogg and writes to out.wav file.

Read: man oggenc

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Sep  1 10:43:17 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Sep  1 23:13:33 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Mailing list guidelines
Message-ID: <20050901174317.12585.qmail@web50211.mail.yahoo.com>

Greetings!

Please don't reply to this e-mail.

This is a reminder to members of this list about the
posting rules:

1. Do not top-post

Example of a top-post:

  I think you should be swapping the arguments around
in the 
  function, instead of the way you are doing it.
  On Friday, the 13th, you said:
  > I am using the function xyz(), giving arguments
arg1 and arg2, 
  > but it does not work. Anyone know why?

Always use bottom-posting.

  On Friday, the 13th, you said:
  > I am using the function xyz(), giving arguments
arg1 and arg2, 
  > but it does not work. Anyone know why?
  I think you should be swapping the arguments around
in the 
  function, instead of the way you are doing it.

Check this link:

http://www.caliburn.nl/topposting.html

2. Do not over-quote

Example of an over-quote:

  >>> On Friday you said
  >>> blah blah blah
  >> On Saturday you said
  >> foo foo foo
  > On Sunday you said
  > foobar

3. Do not post HTML messages

4. Do not recycle messages

5. Do not send attachments

6. Do not attach obnoxious, nonsensical legal
disclaimers

  If your company uses disclaimers, don't use your
company ID for the mailing list.

7. Do not post off-topic messages

8. Do not reply to a digest. (If you are in digest
mode and want to reply to a post use our blog
interface
(http://blog.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc))

If any of the above are not clear to you, please read
the detailed list rules:

  http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/smart-questions.html

Hi,

I am assuming your adsl modem connects with the system
via ethernet.

--- Parth <parth.technofreak@gmail.com> wrote:
> when i giv 
> /sbin/adsl-start ( as well as /sbin/inup ppp0). 

You should use:

  adsl-start eth0 username@dataone

to connect. Replace eth0, username accordingly.

> when
> i checked the system 
> log, it showed some insmod error. 

Post the output of the following before you connect:

/sbin/lspci
/sbin/ifconfig -a

Is the LED light on the ethernet?

Hi Parth,

--- Parth <parth.technofreak@gmail.com> wrote:
> 00.08.0  Ethernet Controler : RealTek Semiconductor
> Co., Ltd. RTL -
> 8139/8139c/8139c+ (rev 10)

Should use 8139too drivers.
 
> output of " /sbin/ifconfig -a "
> 
> lo      Link encap: Local Loopback

You don't have a driver. Hence, there is no eth0 in
the output.
 
/lib/modules/2.4.20-8/kernel/drivers/net/epic100.0:init_module:
> insmod eth0 failed

Its trying to load the intel driver. Can you check in
/lib/modules/2.4.20-8/ (and in drivers/net) for
8139too driver?

If you don't have it then you will need to:

a. recompile kernel with realtek support

or

b. compile the realtex drivers separately from the
source code

From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Sep  2 20:43:55 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (WHICH)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509021935170.2951-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Want to know the Linux News On Internet Time ?? Check Linux Today.
URL: http://linuxtoday.com/

One Day One Command 
===================

which -- Shows the location of (shell) commands.

Summary:

which will search for the given command in the PATH and prints the
full path of the executables that would have been executed when this
command had been entered at the shell prompt.

Examples:

$ which ls -- Print the 1st matching location and alias.

$ which -a kill -- Print all matchings. 

$ which --skip-alias ls -- Don't print the ls alias.

$ which --skip-dot gcc -- Skip Dirs in PATH that start with a dot.

$ which --skip-tilde test -- Skip Dirs in PATH that start with a tilde
                  and executables which reside in the HOME directory.

$ which ls rm cp -- Search for multiple commands.

$ which NoCmd -- Just Try..

Read: man which

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

--- Parth <parth.technofreak@gmail.com> wrote:
> Shakthi,
> Can u tell me how to do the "b" option, i havent
> done anething like that :(

Its time to learn!

> there was one
> available for kernal version 2.4.x for RH9.0, i 
> downloaded it.. its
> 8139cp.zip. Will it workout ?

.zip?

Check this:
http://www.scyld.com/rtl8139.html

You will need your kernel sources installed in your
system. Usually they will be in
/usr/src/linux-<version>. In your case, it will be
/usr/src/linux-2.4.20-8 or something.

One of the many things that newbies don't do while
doing a GNU/Linux installation is not install:

a. development tools
b. kernel sources

You can install the kernel sources from the
installation CDs.

Follow the instructions given in the link for driver
compilation and loading, and ask specific questions if
you are not able to proceed.

Regards,

Subject: [Ilugc] Compiling from tarballs in Ubuntu

Hi,

--- Sudharshan S <sudharsh@gmail.com> wrote:
> hi all,
> i removed my fc3 (BIG MISTAKE) 

Yup. I will definitely recommend FC3. 

> good at handling debian based distros, 

Yeah, you really shouldn't be "handling" distros. Just
use them.

> so when i
> start to install
> softwares from my software archives, 

How?

If you are compiling from source, you only need to do
"./configure; make".

Only "make install" will move the executables to PATH
that might affect the package management repository of
your distro.

> i m having
> trouble from tarballs in
> ubuntu. i m getting an error that glib was not
> found, 

Can you post the error? You might want to use -L in
the Makefile or set LIBS to point to the existing one.

> after modifying my
> 'ld.so.conf' file. this is true even for zlib. 

You really shouldn't be touching these files, unless
and until you are really, really sure on what you are
doing.

From kmshiva at gmail.com  Fri Sep  2 22:27:52 2005
From: kmshiva at gmail.com (Shiva KM)
Date: Fri Sep  2 22:28:02 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Compiling from tarballs in Ubuntu
In-Reply-To: <43186F67.1040907@gmail.com>
References: <43186F67.1040907@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <654433ee050902095745d5c4c1@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

> i removed my fc3 (BIG MISTAKE) and replaced it with ubuntu. 

Well, the ubuntu package manager(i.e. synaptic) is pretty good, and
contains most packages that u wud want - read the 'Extra Repositories'
section in www.ubuntuguide.org to make hte available package database
even bigger. Using the package manager is really easy.

> 'ld.so.conf' file. this is true even for zlib. here are the contents of
> the ld.so.conf
> *********
> /usr/X12R6/lib
> /usr/local/lib
> /usr/lib
> *********

Well, normally u wudn't need to modify ld.so.conf, unless u r
installing libs in an unconventional location, for example I have some
libs in /opt/lib, which I added to ld.so.conf.

Doing a 'ldconfig -p' should give u list of all the libs ldconfig
knows about, see if glib is present in that. On my ubuntu machine, I
seem to have glib 1.2.10 installed.

Would also recommend getting checkinstall, so that u can easily
uninstall packages installed from source.

HTH.
-- 
Thanks and Regards,
shiva
--
Avoid the Gates of Hell.  Use Linux

On Fri, Sep 02, 2005 at 08:57:35PM +0530, Sudharshan S wrote:
> hi all,
> i removed my fc3 (BIG MISTAKE) and replaced it with ubuntu. i m not that
> good at handling debian based distros, so when i start to install
> softwares from my software archives, i m having trouble from 
> tarballs in ubuntu. i m getting an error that glib was not found, so 
> i downloaded a dev version of the same, no effect. gnome does need 
> glib,doesn't it? then why the hell is it not getting detected even 
> after modifying my 'ld.so.conf' file. this is true even for zlib. 
> here are the contents of the ld.so.conf ********* /usr/X12R6/lib 

Well, since Ubuntu is a Debian derivative, you should be apt-getting, wherever
possible, unless that package isn't available in Ubuntu or you have some
special requirement (in which case you can still apt-get get source... but
that's a different matter...)

> checking for glib-config... /usr/bin/glib-config
> checking for GLIB - version >= 1.2.2... no

In Debian, apt-get install libglib1.2-dev will solve this.

And, about XMMS, I can't imagine Ubuntu not having xmms, so you can just say
apt-get install xmms as well.

HTH.

Kumar

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Sun Sep  4 16:47:38 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sun Sep  4 16:46:44 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (NICE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509041619070.12900-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

The Linux Cookbook provides lot of Tips and Techniques for Everyday 
Use. This book is available in On-Line and Printed form.
URL: http://dsl.org/cookbook/

One Day One Command 
===================

nice -- Run a command with modified priority.

Summary:

GNU/Linux is a multi-user and multi-tasking OS. So many processes will
be running with some scheduling policy like Round Rabin, FIFO etc..
High priority process will get more CPU Time.

nice command is used to run the given command with its scheduling
priority adjusted. Priority range goes from -20 (highest priority) 
to 19 (lowest priority).

Examples:

$ nice -- Prints the current priority value.

$ nice ls -- Increment the priority value of the ls command 
             by 10 (Default value) and run.

$ nice -n 5 ls -- Increment the priority value of the ls command
                  by 5 and run.

# nice -n -2 ls -- Decrement the priority value of the ls command by 
                   -2 and run.

NOTE: Incrementing the priority value will reduce the priority level 
      and vice versa. Priority range is -20 (high) to 19 (low).

Read: man nice

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From citizenofgnu at gmail.com  Mon Sep  5 01:17:57 2005
From: citizenofgnu at gmail.com (Thyagu rajan)
Date: Mon Sep  5 01:18:06 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Guidelines for software freedom day from
	Softwarefreedomday.org
Message-ID: <ed2d3c0005090412472a3c0c87@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Friends,
The following are the guidelines prescribed by the 
www.softwarefreedomday.org <http://www.softwarefreedomday.org>, Volunteers 
are requested to go through and have these points noted.


Some guidelines to make SFD a positive celebration:


   - DO present the capabilities and practical benefits of FOSS.


   - DO NOT pretend that FOSS is perfect for everyone or everything.



   - DO have the ability to present FOSS ideology clearly and concisely 
   to interested people.


   - DO NOT beat uninterested people over the head with ideology; this 
   will confuse and intimidate them. Instead...
   


   - DO let the quality of the software speak for itself and its 
   ideology.



   - DO have demo machines present if possible.



   - DO your best to connect people with a local FOSS community.



   - DO provide contact information for your SFD team so people can 
   subsequently contact you for

more information.


   - DO get contact information from interested and willing people, so 
   you can proactively follow-up with them later.



   - DO proactively follow-up with people who attend your SFD event.



   - DO find and cooperate with other SFD teams in your area.



   - DO start other SFD teams in your area - this cooperation, not 
   competition!



   - DO NOT -- seriously -- DO NOT bash Microsoft or SCO or any other 
   false Great Satan.
<http://www.gnu.org/philosophy/microsoft.html>Software Freedom Day is
not about any individual companies or people;
   Software Freedom Day is a positive community celebration of Software 
   Freedom.




Cheers,


Thyagarajan Shanmugham

to our clients / business partners and their business
/ certification needs. Identify the gaps at policy &
implementation levels and provide suitable remedial 
action plans.

On a day-to-day basis, the qualified candidate will
provide technical guidance to the Information Systems
Department. The selected candidate will act as a
technical resource to associates, IT managers and 
departmental heads.

The candidate will need to be customer focused and
highly analytical with the willingness to learn new
skills. Self-motivated, adaptable and change
oriented, you will also be a confident communicator 
both written and verbal with the ability to deliver
seminars and awareness programs to large audiences.
Must be an excellent team player and should have the
ability to lead small to moderate sized teams.

RESPONSIBILITIES:
-----------------
- Assist in development / revision of information
security policies of the organization towards
achieving a certification status.

- Assist in developing, implementing, and maintaining an 
ongoing Information Security awareness and employee
training program for various levels of the
organization.

- Provide technical assistance in the selection,
configuration, and maintenance of security software, 
utilities and hardware.

- Assist in the development of technical security
standards to support policies including assisting in
creating and coordinating monitoring standards and
incident investigation procedures. 

- Conduct periodic OS and application security
assessments and reviews for evidence of vulnerability
or compromise and assist in and or facilitate the
implementation of resolution. Tracks resolution of
findings and prepare reports.

- Respond to and report on IT security incidents,
provide initial assessment of impact severity and
types of incidences being addressed. Coordinates
resolution efforts with Information Security Manager 
for critical or serious incidents.

- Monitor network & servers and security appliances for
evidence of compromise and report security incidents.
Analyze compromised resource to assist in improving
security design, policy compliance, and to understand
and document new threat profiles.

- Monitor and enforces compliance with security
policies, standards and guidelines.

- Keeps current on security issues and report issues to 
the IT and other department personnel responsible for
the resource.


CERTIFICATIONS & SKILLS:
------------------------
Preferred: MCSE, CNA, CISA, CISSP, SANS, etc. Aware
of certification standards such as HIPPA, BS7799:2, 
ISO17999

EDUCATIONAL REQUIREMENT
-----------------------
Bachelors Degree in CS or Engineering with 5+ years
training in information technology, information
security. MBA or management experience will be a plus. 

MINIMUM EXPERIENCE
------------------
Experience in information technology support and or
auditing information technology in diverse,
centralized / decentralized environments with
progressively increasing responsibilities. 

Experience with the network and server hardware,
software with a focus on security implementation and
security tools for diverse platforms.

Skills: Thorough knowledge of Micro$oft(!) & Un*X (at
least one flavor of it) and Linux for both server & 
desktop. Thorough knowledge of one hardware and one
software firewall, IDP, IPS, Virus scanning gateways,

hi parth,

wht does ifup eth0 say, since u have the drivers check if u have the alias 
defined in 

/etc/modules.conf 

or

/etc/modprobe.conf

it should have an entry like this,


alias eth0 8139too

also check the /etc/sysconfig/network-scripts/ifcfg-eth0
can u post both the above files.


i don't think recompiling is necessary.



regards,

kiran

detected' and asks if i want to load drivers from a floppy. Of course, i 
don't have  floppy drive. :)

It comes preloaded with Linpus Linux and
dmesg gives
Philips CD-RW/DVD-ROM SCB5265
Uniform CD-ROM driver Revision: 3.20

The great Google pointed me to a few postings where folks said that it 
has something to do with sata and ati_piix and advised a change in the 
BIOS from SATA Automatic to Enhanced. The only problem is Acer ships it 
with a cheapo bios that does not allow me to do all this.

me proceed with an install (I aborted it after the CD-ROM detect step).

From srsy70 at gmail.com  Tue Sep  6 18:54:59 2005
From: srsy70 at gmail.com (S.Ramaswamy)
Date: Tue Sep  6 18:55:12 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Reg Having More than one CVS repository
In-Reply-To: <001801c5b2d3$647dd960$7201a8c0@Pranesh>
References: <001801c5b2d3$647dd960$7201a8c0@Pranesh>
Message-ID: <d60e5b0f05090606247a19d9b4@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/6/05, Praneshkrishnan <pranesh@trioztech.com> wrote:
> 
> Dear Group
> 
> Is it possible to have more than one CVS running on the same PC at the 
> Same time.


You can, by adding the cvs repository roots to the --allow-root option in 
your /etc/xinetd.d/cvspserver file. I am assuming here that you are running 
a pserver with xinetd. The syntax is pretty much the same with tcpserver 
etc. Here's a sample /etc/xinetd.d/cvspserver

service cvspserver
{
socket_type = stream
protocol = tcp
wait = no
user = root
passenv = PATH
server = /usr/bin/cvs
server_args = -f --allow-root=/opt/repos/project1 
--allow-root=/opt/repos/project2 pserver
}

HTH
Ramaswamy

From kbalavignesh at gmail.com  Thu Sep  8 12:18:37 2005

Subject: [Ilugc] Re-Reg Having More than one CVS repository
Message-ID: <bc3fff5205090723483af6bd9e@mail.gmail.com>

Praneshkrishnan wrote

>                    Is it possible to have more than one CVS running on >the same PC at the Same time.

 It is possible and simple. Just Import the Project/Directory to the
CVSROOT. (dont give existing name).

I think u confused among the difference betn CVSROOT and CVS repository....

Both are called repository but for ur clarification consider

if $CVSROOT=/home/cvsrepos    then You can import more than one
projects/modules/repository/subrepository   what ever u called.
but while import u have to give different name.

while checkout 
 #cvs checkout <repository name>

while any other command (from client side), if ur inside the directory  
no need to mention the repository name.

(Every directory contains CVS/Repository file it will take care of all the
Details)

For More information http://cvsbook.red-bean.com/cvsbook.html

Regards

Balavignesh

from your target system. Replace /usr/src/linux with

From fred at bytesforall.org  Thu Sep  8 14:12:45 2005
From: fred at bytesforall.org (Frederick Noronha (FN))
Date: Thu Sep  8 14:04:28 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] A Frenchman, and maps ... in the South Pacific
Message-ID: <1126168965.3866.18.camel@localhost.localdomain>

A Frenchman, and maps ... in the South Pacific

Franck Martin [1] is a Frenchman based in the South Pacific. (You might
have noticed his sense of humour on the trip to Angkor Wat.) As a
Wikipedia contributor, he's described as someone "checking mainly the
pages of the Pacific Islands and updating when neccessary. Promotion of
wikipedia in Pacific Islands." But what's more interesting is his
Tikimaps [2] work.

http://www.iosn.net/events/fossap-2005/blog/franck

Mapserver, says Franck, is a tool, for "bringing data to all
stakeholders via Internet and Opensource Technology". It promises the
tools for e-government, good governance, transparency, sustainable
development, asset management, disaster management and security....
provided we have the political will for that. 

To see what's possible, visit some of these sites from the distant (from
us!) South Pacific islands of Tonga [3], Fiji [4], Tuvalu [5], Kiribati
[6]. Franck sees many advantages in using Free and Open Source software.
These include sustainability, licenses (Internet licences are
expensives), software support, no "black box" phenomenon (where we don't
understand the technology we use). It also allows you to rely on
standards and support many file formats (not vendor dependent). It is
reliable. And secure too, provided the administrator cares for it.

For more links on what uses Tikiwiki can be put to take a look at the
Tikiwiki Community Portal [7]. Uses include uses in educational context
[8], using the mobility features of WAP browsing or for use with a PDA
[9], and, of course, Franck's interest of maps [10].  -- Frederick
Noronha

[1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User:Franck_Martin
[2] http://maps.tikiwiki.org/
[3] http://www.lands.gov.to/tiki/tiki-map.phtml?mapfile=tonga.map
[4] http://map.mrd.gov.fj/tiki/tiki-map.phtml?mapfile=viti.map
[5] http://map.tuvalu.tv/tiki/tiki-map.phtml
[6] http://map.gov.ki/tiki/tiki-map.phtml?mapfile=tarawa.map
[7] http://tikiwiki.org/
[8] http://edu.tikiwiki.org/tiki-index.php
[9] http://mobile.tikiwiki.org/tiki-index.php
[10]http://maps.tikiwiki.org/tiki-index.php
--

From fred at bytesforall.org  Fri Sep  9 01:37:55 2005
From: fred at bytesforall.org (Frederick Noronha (FN))
Date: Fri Sep  9 01:29:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] A million rupees in prizes... Collabnet is hiring... India's
	listed user groups touch 139...
Message-ID: <1126210075.3866.365.camel@localhost.localdomain>

IT MIGHT BE a bit too late to talk about an August-datelined issue of a
magazine, but ... better late than never.

          Just to highlight some of what one found interesting in the
          AUGUST 2005 issue of Linux For You magazine. Send in your
          comments and feedback to lfyedit@efyindia.org 

          INDIA IS BEGINNING to contribute to the global FLOSS pool,
          and thereby erasing the stain of being just a net taker
          rather than a net contributor. Results are just in from the
          first Code Scholarship challenge, initiated by the
          Kanwal Rekhi School of Information Technology (KreSIT),
          IIT Bombay, and Red Hat India. It is designed to encourage
          FLOSS developers in India. Some 2000 students registered.
          Finally, 34 teams bagged awards. First was VPS 1.6.0
          (Virtual Private Server) developed by the Army Institute
          of Technology, Pune. Next was Octave-GTK by the
          National Institute of Technology, Tiruchirapalli; and
          ranked third was a College Information System, developed by
          the Institute of Engineering & Technology, Hyderabad.
          Prizes totalled a million rupees in all (Rs 10 lakh!)

* An advert from Collabnet says it is hiring people with over five 
  years experience in developing or testing web-based enterprise
  applications. See http://www.collab.net/cspl.html
* Multi-boot your system with dual hard disks. Install and 
  experiment with multiple distributions on one system, which has 
  two hard disks.
* Sri Lanka is having a series of major Free/Libre and 
  Open Source Software events. See http://www.fosssl.org
* Mandrive Limited Edition 2005. 
* Intel Compilers 9.0 for Linux
* Communication between independent processes by FIFO.
* An interview: Jim Stallings, general manager Linux of IBM.
* Working with databases in Mono. See how to connect to and query
  a database in Mono, as it can communicate with almost all FOSS
  and commercial databases.
* BEA brings Java onto Linux. 
* vsftp -- securing your data behind seven walls.
* Easy database development using Rekall.
* JCodeFlow, debugging made easy.By Raja RK
* Apache for PHP Developers (Part I). By Nirav Mehta.
* Sunbird and iCalendar. Sharing calendars. By Reuven
  M Lerner, courtesy Linux Journal.
* Administering Linux Systems. By Sanjay Gupta, Novell, Bangalore.
* Network Simulator: an open source design and testing tool. 
  Aniket Jain.
* Object creation and garbage collection in Java. By
  Lakshmi Narayanan N of HCL Technologies.
* Blocks functions in Ruby. By Premshree Pillai. Technical Yahoo!
* XML Python Part II. By Anand Pillai, H-P India.
* Backups in a Snap with rsnapshot. Nilayam Sharma.Silicon Valley.

USER GROUPS IN INDIA: Currently, the list spreads over two pages (a few
which I tried to check out had bad links though). From 80+ the number of
LUGs, FSUGs and GLUGs has grown to 139! Next challenge: let's keep them
active! 

FOR NEWBIES: * Learn how to use Mozilla, the popular Web browser, to
find information on the Net. * GIMP, a great image enhancement tool. Get
exposed to GIMP and design whatever you want to.

Brief updates:
* PHP 4.4.0 is released
* Qt 4.0 is now available
* Firefox 1.5 on its way

TOP TEN [GNU]LINUX GIZMOS: Motorola E680i [1] smartphone with 2GB
storage camera and touch-screen; Samsung's multi-functional device
called the Minikit [2] (camcoder, digital camera, MP3 player,
voice-recorder, memory stick and Web cam!); Archos' Pocket Media
Assistant PMA400 [3] with a 30GB hard drive, wireless Internet
connectivity and direct video recording capability from TV; and Sony
Ericsson's robotic camera ROB-1 [4] packed with a VGA camera and four
LEDs.

There's also the TomTomGo [5], Linux-based in-car GPS navigation system;
Jentro Technologies GmbH (Germany) Jentro Car [6] central technology
platform for the network and control of in-car functions of a Mercedes;
Citizen Watch and IBM Research's WatchPad [7]; Smartvue home security
and surveillance system [8]; all-in-one AmstradE3 videophone [9] (to
send email, SMS/MMS messages, surf the net and videoconference);
GNU/Linux-powered broadband terminal/IP phone [10] from MontaVista.

          EMBEDDED LINUX gadgets are doing great in Asia, specially
          in Japan, China and Taiwan, where major players like
          NTT DoCoMo and NEC are endorsing the GNU/Linux OS.
          Encore Software Ltd, the makers of the Simputer
          http://www.ncoretech.com and signup at
          http://groups.yahoo.com/group/simputer announced recently
          plans to launch another GNU/Linux handheld called
          Mobilis, a "mobile desktop". Mobilis family of products
          includes Mobilis STN, Mobils TFT and Mobilis SofComp.
          The first two are tablet computers, that can bridge the
          gap between PDAs and laptops. SofComp is a low-cost desktop.

THIN DOWN ON [GNU]LINUX: Linux may be struggling to break Microsoft's
stranglehold on the desktop, but the thinner, leaner and meaner thin
clients based on the [GNU]Linux OS are fast becoming the choice of both
public and private enterprise. Some popular GNU/Linux thin clients are
HP t5525 and t5125, Neoware Capio One and Eon, Netvoyager Lithium
LX-104- and LX-1030 and LX-1020, Wyse Winterm 5150SE.

SOFTWARE ON THE CDs: MRBS or Meeting Room Booking Schedules; Alfresco
for content management, Firefox, Xine, ackerTodo (Web-based to-do list
manager), XMMS, D4X (download manager), BMDFM (binary modular dataflow
machine), GIMP (GNU image manipulation programme), Pavuk (to mirror
contents of WWW documents or files), Pundict (open source Punjabi
dictionary for the Windows platform), PyPE (Python programming editor
for the Windows platform), pxlib (simple and small C library to read and
write), LibGTop (fetches system related info like CPU load, memory
usage, etc), Xandros 3.0 OCE, easy to install.

>http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc

>
Linux:
"dmesg" gives you complete hardware detected details during kernel 
loading. It is useful for debugging.
lsusb - lists all usb devices
lspci - lists all pci devices in your system. since today's machines 
uses mostly pci devices, it lists most of the devices in the system
Other Unix:
"hwconfig" - runs on unix system ( i have seen in sco-unix), u can try 
that in other unices also.

Dear All,

On Sep 10th, ILUGC (We) planned to celebrate the IInd World Software
Freedom Day (SFD) by conducting two programs at TNSTC  (Tamil Nadu
Science and Technological Centre),  Birla Planetarium  Complex,
Kotturpuram, CH- 25.

Today, The Hindu is added this news in the "Around the City"  Column,
Page 3.

1. One Day FOSS Training Program for 50 School Teachers.
2. Linux Demo Day, Open to All.

Instructions:-

1. Reach the LDD place by 8AM.
2. If you bring your PC, Write down the components list
   in a plain paper and show to the security.
3. Bring the Extension power boxes.
4. If you have extra Distro CDs, bring it for free distributions.
5. Thous who can't spend full day in LDD, can come there for
   1 or 2hrs in morning to help setting the stalls.

Still We need 2 or 3 PCs. If you are free, Plz join with us with your
PC.

From rudyandlinda at yahoo.com  Sat Sep 10 20:53:51 2005
From: rudyandlinda at yahoo.com (Rudy Colbert)
Date: Sun Sep 11 09:24:11 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Command to find out hardare information
Message-ID: <20050911035351.30952.qmail@web52510.mail.yahoo.com>


>>> Hello all,
Are there any commands or utilites in Linux, by which
one can find out
the complete hardware information etc about a system
running, <<<

Yes.  'dmidecode' written by Alan Cox.

Dmidecode reports information about your system's
hardware as described in your system BIOS according to
the SMBIOS/DMI standard (see a sample output). This
information typically includes system manufacturer,
model name, serial number, BIOS version, asset tag as
well as a lot of other details of varying level of
interest and reliability depending on the
manufacturer. This will often include usage status for
the CPU sockets, expansion slots (e.g. AGP, PCI, ISA)
and memory module slots, and the list of I/O ports
(e.g. serial, parallel, USB).

http://www.nongnu.org/dmidecode/

Sample output below ....

# dmidecode 2.2
SMBIOS 2.1 present.
26 structures occupying 771 bytes.
Table at 0x000F1070.

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Sun Sep 11 20:01:09 2005

Subject: [Ilugc] Software Freedom Day
Message-ID: <f480bf1e05091107313aa291c1@mail.gmail.com>

It struck me that "Software Freedom" may mean several things,
including the idea that people have the freedom to lawfully acquire
and use any software they like.  Perhaps, it is this meaning that
should be higlighted on Software Freedom Day in future, so that it may
be celebrated by one and all in a spirit of brotherhood.  Recognising
the freedom to use any software we like would also mean that all have
a chance to be treated alike, and no person would be criticised for
his individual choice of software.  I feel this may become
increasingly apparent in the days to come.

FYI, Microsoft is governed by the American law on vicarious liability for the action of its vendors;In simple Indian terms, when you find an american outfit practising "vendor" concepts here, ask the company whether it will honor its "vendor's" committment; they will even give you a written committment. American companies take up the fullest responsibility for their "distributor's" or "vendors" committment to the outside world as if it were made by them, purely on their own.

Subject: [Ilugc] Reg Processors Architectures
In-Reply-To: <001d01c5b5db$b18fe530$7201a8c0@Pranesh>
References: <001d01c5b5db$b18fe530$7201a8c0@Pranesh>
Message-ID: <8e6637b5050911212154ae45a6@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/10/05, Praneshkrishnan <pranesh@trioztech.com> wrote:
> 
> RISC       ->    PIC , ARM
> 
> CISC       - >    8051

Add to that EPIC (Exposed Paralled Instruction Computer) which
includes the IA64.
Also, VLIW (though you can't put it in the same category as RISC/CISC)
which include the Transmeta's Crusoe (Linus worked there before he
went fulltime to OSDL).

If you are looking at computer architecture, try to get your hands on
Hennessy and Patterson (both the books). Tanenbaum is good for basics.

regards
Vishnu Vyas

 The Software Freedom Day celebrations went on well on 10th sep 2005.
Highlight of the day are
1. The seminar to School teachers: Nearly 40 teachers from about 25
schools attended the seminar. The sessions covered were -
Introduction to FOSS,HSC school Linux syllabus and installation.
2. There were roughly 80-90 visitors
3. There was unannounced seminar to over 60 students from Balaji
polytechnic. What is realy great about the students was - almost  99%
of them are using Linux - a fact totaly opposite to situations in
many   engg colleges. We have asked them to organise local LUG.


Overall it was very stasifying. 

 On behalf of ILUGC, I thank Dr.Iyamperumal,ED,TNSTC  for giving us
excellent facility, publicity and for co-ordination with schools for
delegates to the seminar. One additonal special thanks for arranging
excellent lunch. We thank the team of Scientific Officers and others
of TNSTC for the help they gave us.

From trshash84 at gmail.com  Mon Sep 12 11:24:32 2005
From: trshash84 at gmail.com (T.R.Shashwath)
Date: Mon Sep 12 11:23:56 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Request for Gentoo
In-Reply-To: <7c6561690509112109160de385@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7c6561690509112109160de385@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200509121124.33261.trshash84@gmail.com>

I have the universal (I think), but you have to keep a few things in mind - 
Live CD or no, to install, you still have to download all the packages from 
the Net. That in itself comes to two CDs, and that's not counting the portage 
updates. If you truly want to try it out, you need a connection with at least 
2 GB/month downloads, and preferably unlimited downloads. If you have this, I 
suggest that you download the minimal livecd (about 60 megs) and go on. 
Otherwise, Gentoo may not be right for you.

Also, Gentoo "releases" are only for the livecd, and not the distro itself. 
The distro is in a permanent state of update, and you can install an older 
'version' (as in install using an older livecd) and keep upto date without 
ever reinstalling, like you would with other distros. I took my system from 
1.4 RC 4 to 2004.something, and kept that running till about a couple of 
months back. I only reinstalled because I changed most of my hardware, and I 
wanted a bit more optimization. In other words, if you have an older livecd, 
just use it.

On Monday 12 September 2005 12:13, Sai Kiran wrote:
> hi,,
>
> i thought Gentoo has a option for networkless install. they call it the
> universal cd.
> the live cd is to be used if u want to download everthing from the net for
> which i don't have the neccessary bandwidth.
>
> Correct me if i am wrong?
>
> regards,
> kiran

The Universal livecd is for installing when you want the base system up and 
running fast. It has the final stage of bootstrapping and installing, from 
where you still have to setup the kernel and compile whatever other programs 
(X windows, your choice of desktop environment, etc) you want.

In other words, even with the universal, you still have to compile about half 
the system.

There is always the possibility of getting the distfiles (sources for 
programs) from friends and compiling them on your system (I've setup one 
system this way - it's running quite well), but that has its own 
complexities. I wouldn't recommend trying that without doing a "normal" 
gentoo install to begin with.

-- 
Shash
---

 create him."
 -Arthur C. Clarke

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Sep 12 19:09:01 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Sep 12 19:07:37 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (RENICE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509121841550.795-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Mr Vijay Kumar released Beta version of XPDF with GGI (General
Graphics Interface) Front end. Use of GGI will give the reliable,
stable and fast graphics system that works everywhere. 
URL: http://www.bravegnu.org/xpdf/  (Volunteers Needed)

One Day One Command 
===================

renice -- Alter priority of running processes.

Summary:

GNU/Linux is a multi-user and multi-tasking OS. So many processes will
be running with some scheduling policy like Round Rabin, FIFO etc..
High priority process will get more CPU Time.

Renice is used to alters the scheduling priority of one or more
running processes. Priority range goes from -20 (highest priority)  
to 19 (lowest priority).

Examples:

$ renice +1 123 -- Increment the priority value of a process, which 
                   process ID is 123.

# renice +1 123 -- Decrement the priority value of a process, which 
                   process ID is 123. (Root only can decrement ).

$ renice +1 -p 123 -p 200 -- Same as above. Here no. of process is 2.

$ renice +1 -u sbharathi -- Increment the priority value of all 
                     processes, which is owned by a user (sbharathi).

$ renice +1 -g backup -- Increment the priority value of all
               processes, which is owned by a group (backup).


NOTE: Incrementing the priority value will reduce the priority level 
      and vice versa. Priority range is -20 (high) to 19 (low).

Read: man renice

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

            I have some doubt in interrupthandlers.the
coding which is have shown below is taken form the
book 
"LINUX KERNEL MODULAR PROGRAMMING".
         



#include <linux/kernel.h>               /* We're doing
kernel work */
#include <linux/module.h>               /*
Specifically, a module */
#include <linux/sched.h>
#include <linux/tqueue.h>
#include <linux/interrupt.h>
#include <asm/io.h>

static void got_char(void *scancode)
{
   printk("Scan Code %x %s.\n",
          (int) *((char *) scancode) & 0x7F,
          *((char *) scancode) & 0x80 ? "Released" :
"Pressed");
}

void irq_handler(int irq, void *dev_id, struct pt_regs
*regs)
{
   static unsigned char scancode;
   static struct tq_struct task = {NULL, 0, got_char,
&scancode};
   unsigned char status;


   status = inb(0x64);
   scancode = inb(0x60);
  
   queue_task_irq(&task, &tq_immediate);
   mark_bh(IMMEDIATE_BH);
}

/* Initialize the module - register the IRQ handler */
int init_module()
{
   free_irq(1, NULL);

   return request_irq(1,   /* The number of the
keyboard IRQ on PCs */ 
              irq_handler, /* our handler */
              SA_SHIRQ, 
              "test_keyboard_irq_handler", NULL);
}

/* Cleanup */
void cleanup_module()
{
   free_irq(1, NULL);
}  

    Problem:

             The problem is this program is compiled.
there is no problem in compilation.when the module is
load using insmod command, the system will be hang +
the keyboard(numlock,capslock,scrolllock)all are
blinking.

          i know what to do any body plz help me

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Sep 13 20:01:37 2005

Date: Tue Sep 13 19:59:51 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (WHATIS)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509131945060.10993-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Mr Vijay Kumar B released Beta version of XPDF with GGI (General
Graphics Interface) Front end. Use of GGI will give a reliable,
stable and fast graphics system that works everywhere. 
URL: http://www.bravegnu.org/xpdf/  (Developers Needed)

One Day One Command 
===================

whatis -- Search the whatis database for complete words.

Summary:

Whatis DB contains the name and one line description about all
commands man pages. whatis searches for keywords and displays the
result(s) on the standard output. Only complete word matches are
displayed.

Examples:

$ whatis ls -- Show small info about ls command.

$ whatis perl -- Show small info about perl.

$ whatis gcc -- Show small info about gcc command.

$ whatis printf -- Show small info about printf.

$ whatis socket -- Show small info about socket.

$ whatis compile -- Just try (Error).

Read: man whatis

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

Rudy Colbert wrote:
>>>>Hello all,
> 
> Are there any commands or utilites in Linux, by which
> one can find out
> the complete hardware information etc about a system
> running, <<<
> 
> Yes.  'dmidecode' written by Alan Cox.
> 
> Dmidecode reports information about your system's
> hardware as described in your system BIOS according to
> the SMBIOS/DMI standard (see a sample output). This
> information typically includes system manufacturer,
> model name, serial number, BIOS version, asset tag as
> well as a lot of other details of varying level of
> interest and reliability depending on the
> manufacturer. This will often include usage status for
> the CPU sockets, expansion slots (e.g. AGP, PCI, ISA)
> and memory module slots, and the list of I/O ports
> (e.g. serial, parallel, USB).
> 
> http://www.nongnu.org/dmidecode/
> 
> Sample output below ....
>

Hello Prem:

A lot of people seem to be searching for elusive 965L drivers.   I found 
a patch reference below  from Linux development archives.
http://ftp.kernel.org/pub/linux/kernel/v2.6/snapshots/patch-2.6.13-git4.log 
- the bit below is my cutout. 

Not sure if you were planning this for Linux or FreeBSD but 99% of the 
code should be similar.. if you know where to find it?

Good luck and good on you!

Graham/
Vancouver, Canada.

If you are lucky with this I would love see the finished product, maybe 
I can figure out how to compile into my FreeBSD kernel.
 

[PATCH] sis190: resurrection
    
    Raise the sis190 driver from the dead
    
    The driver handles the integrated network device found on SiS 965L
    chipset. It follows the classical (non-napi) interrupt-driven model
    and provides minimal ethtool support.
    
    The code comes from a heavy cleanup/rewrite of the original code
    which was removed from the kernel on 14/04/2004. Since the r8169
    driver does not work too bad and there will probably be (at least)
    a few months of improvements/testing/fixing, I made the code as
    close as possible to the r8169 one.
    
    Pascal Chapperon <pascal.chapperon@wanadoo.fr> deserves some special
    credit for testing and bug-catching. Many thanks to Lars Vahlenberg
    as well.

 "I have one program which is taken from linux kernel
modular programming.While compilation there was no
error,but i could'nt run the program.when i tried to

and the keyboard LED's was blinking".why such problem
arise? 

          this my doubt.i don't know how to specify my
doubt to kernel experts.

        



coding:

   /*  intrpt.c - An interrupt handler.
 *
 *  Copyright (C) 2001 by Peter Jay Salzman
 */

/* The necessary header files */

/* Standard in kernel modules */
#include <linux/kernel.h>               /* We're doing
kernel work */
#include <linux/module.h>               /*
Specifically, a module */

/* Deal with CONFIG_MODVERSIONS */
#if CONFIG_MODVERSIONS==1
#define MODVERSIONS
#include <linux/modversions.h>
#endif        

#include <linux/sched.h>
#include <linux/tqueue.h>

/* We want an interrupt */
#include <linux/interrupt.h>

#include <asm/io.h>

/* In 2.2.3 /usr/include/linux/version.h includes a
macro for this, but
 * 2.0.35 doesn't - so I add it here if necessary.
 */
#ifndef KERNEL_VERSION
#define KERNEL_VERSION(a,b,c) ((a)*65536+(b)*256+(c))
#endif

/* Bottom Half - this will get called by the kernel as
soon as it's safe
 * to do everything normally allowed by kernel
modules.
 */
static void got_char(void *scancode)
{
   printk("Scan Code %x %s.\n",
          (int) *((char *) scancode) & 0x7F,
          *((char *) scancode) & 0x80 ? "Released" :
"Pressed");
}

/* This function services keyboard interrupts. It
reads the relevant
 * information from the keyboard and then scheduales
the bottom half
 * to run when the kernel considers it safe.
 */
void irq_handler(int irq, void *dev_id, struct pt_regs
*regs)
{
   /* This variables are static because they need to
be 
    * accessible (through pointers) to the bottom half
routine.
    */
   static unsigned char scancode;
   static struct tq_struct task = {NULL, 0, got_char,
&scancode};
   unsigned char status;

   /* Read keyboard status */
   status = inb(0x64);
   scancode = inb(0x60);
  
   /* Scheduale bottom half to run */
#if LINUX_VERSION_CODE > KERNEL_VERSION(2,2,0)
   queue_task(&task, &tq_immediate);
#else
   queue_task_irq(&task, &tq_immediate);
#endif
   mark_bh(IMMEDIATE_BH);
}

/* Initialize the module - register the IRQ handler */
int init_module()
{
   /* Since the keyboard handler won't co-exist with
another handler,
    * such as us, we have to disable it (free its IRQ)
before we do
    * anything.  Since we don't know where it is,
there's no way to
		* reinstate it later - so the computer will have to
be rebooted
		* when we're done.
    */
   free_irq(1, NULL);

   /* Request IRQ 1, the keyboard IRQ, to go to our
irq_handler.
	  * SA_SHIRQ means we're willing to have othe
handlers on this IRQ.
		* SA_INTERRUPT can be used to make the handler into
a fast interrupt. 
    */
   return request_irq(1,   /* The number of the
keyboard IRQ on PCs */ 
              irq_handler, /* our handler */
              SA_SHIRQ, 
              "test_keyboard_irq_handler", NULL);
}

/* Cleanup */
void cleanup_module()
{
   /* This is only here for completeness. It's totally
irrelevant, since
	  * we don't have a way to restore the normal
keyboard interrupt so the
		* computer is completely useless and has to be
rebooted.
    */
   free_irq(1, NULL);
}

From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)

Subject: [Ilugc] Debian [well, ubuntu] package management
Message-ID: <4328FFE7.5030908@frodo.hserus.net>

Be gentle with this newbie. After several years of using slackware, I
just installed Ubuntu (kubuntu hoary which then got upgraded to breezy
with apt-get dist-upgrade, blowing up around 500 megs of my 3 gb a month
bandwidth quota)

Now, I rather like it, the install process is a lot cleaner than the one
Debian has as well.

However, the default 2.6.12-8 kernel with ubuntu breezy (or the 2.6.10
with hoary) has a lot of stuff I don't need, and lacks a bunch of things
(ck, inotify etc) that I do need ..

Further, the ubuntu default kernel has a nasty way of locking things up
on my laptop every few minutes when the load is high enough to go into
swap, while applying ck + inotify patches keep it running smoothly for
me.  Actually, I use the archck patchset (these two plus a few more), as
-cko doesnt seem to be maintained now.

Anyway, I did a "fakeroot make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image" after I
patched stock 2.6.12 and did a make menuconfig, and the new kernel works
just great.  I also installed newer versions of cpufreqd, laptop-mode
-tools and the ipw2200 centrino wifi driver, (using debs available from
their respective websites).

So now all I have to do is to tell apt-get not to try upgrading other
kernels, or downgrading to antique and buggy versions of cpufreqd,
laptop-mode and ipw2200 when I next do an apt-get upgrade.

Short question is - how do I mark certain packages as "don't touch
these, I'll do it by hand" and still stay within debian's remarkably
anal retentive packaging system?

	srs

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Sep 15 00:41:42 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)

Hi,

--- bala murugan <sps_bala@yahoo.com> wrote:

> error,but i could'nt run the program.when i tried to
> load the module i can't load it. the system was
> hanged
> and the keyboard LED's was blinking".

The code is meant to do the above.

It clearly says this in the code itself!

>    /* Since the keyboard handler won't co-exist with
> another handler,
>     * such as us, we have to disable it (free its
> IRQ)
> before we do
>     * anything.  Since we don't know where it is,
> there's no way to
> 		* reinstate it later - so the computer will have
> to
> be rebooted
> 		* when we're done.

You have to reboot.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Sep 15 00:48:19 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Sep 15 13:18:37 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Certification related discussion
In-Reply-To: <4328F9AF.9050407@tandbintl.com>
Message-ID: <20050915074819.41206.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

My thoughts below:

--- "T.KaruppuSwamy" <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
> 1. What is the opinion of ILUGC members on these
> certification?

I don't consider it as a means of proving one's
calibre.

If you can contribute to FLOSS projects at:

http://savannah.gnu.org
http://freshmeat.net
http://sf.net

it will show that you are really capable of
coding/development/testing, and that you can work with
programmers from all around the world.

If you continue to do the above, you will have a means
to show that your skills are uptodate and you are
working on current technologies and cutting edge. 

> 5. What is the contribution of these examination to
> avail a opportunity 
> to get interview call for a linux job in
> India/Chennai?

I can't speak for others.

When you work on R&D, for instance, you can't ask for
certifications, because, you won't even have
documentation when working in this domain. You will
only have code to work with. So, the ability/skill to
understand code and hack it, is important.
Certifications don't reveal such abilities.

Regards,

SK

From thyagarajan at gmail.com  Thu Sep 15 15:55:25 2005

Date: Thu Sep 15 15:55:37 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Some computer terms
Message-ID: <65452863050915032532bcab1a@mail.gmail.com>

COMPUTER  TERMINOLOGY

State-of-the-art 	Any computer you can't afford
Obsolete 	Any computer you own
Microsecond 	The time it takes for your state-of-the-art computer to
become obsolete
Keyboard 	The standard way to generate computer errors
Mouse 	An advanced input device to make computer errors easier to generate
Floppy 	The state of your wallet after purchasing a computer
Portable Computer 	A device invented to force businessmen to work at
home, on vacation, and on business trips
Disk Crash 	A typical computer response to any critical deadline
Power User 	Anyone who can format a disk from SHELL
System Update 	A quick method of trashing ALL of your software

copied from
http://www.computerschool.net/computer/basic.html

Sounds humour.

Cheers

Thyagarajan Shanmugham

> Mr Vijay Kumar B released Beta version of XPDF with GGI (General
> Graphics Interface) Front end. Use of GGI will give a reliable,
> stable and fast graphics system that works everywhere.
> URL: http://www.bravegnu.org/xpdf/  (Developers Needed)
> 
> One Day One Command
> ===================
> 
> whatis -- Search the whatis database for complete words.
> 
> Summary:
> 
> Whatis DB contains the name and one line description about all
> commands man pages. whatis searches for keywords and displays the
> result(s) on the standard output. Only complete word matches are
> displayed.
> 
> Examples:
> 
> $ whatis ls -- Show small info about ls command.
> 
> $ whatis perl -- Show small info about perl.
> 
> $ whatis gcc -- Show small info about gcc command.
> 
> $ whatis printf -- Show small info about printf.
> 
> $ whatis socket -- Show small info about socket.
> 
> $ whatis compile -- Just try (Error).
> 
> Read: man whatis
> 
> HTH :)
> --
> Bharathi S
> ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

> Message: 4

> From: Suresh Ramasubramanian <linux@frodo.hserus.net>
> Subject: [Ilugc] Debian [well, ubuntu] package management
> To: Chennai Linux User's Group <ilugc@ae.iitm.ac.in>
> Message-ID: <4328FFE7.5030908@frodo.hserus.net>
> Content-Type: text/plain; charset=UTF-8
> 
> Be gentle with this newbie. After several years of using slackware, I
> just installed Ubuntu (kubuntu hoary which then got upgraded to breezy
> with apt-get dist-upgrade, blowing up around 500 megs of my 3 gb a month
> bandwidth quota)
> 
> Now, I rather like it, the install process is a lot cleaner than the one
> Debian has as well.
> 
> However, the default 2.6.12-8 kernel with ubuntu breezy (or the 2.6.10
> with hoary) has a lot of stuff I don't need, and lacks a bunch of things
> (ck, inotify etc) that I do need ..
> 
> Further, the ubuntu default kernel has a nasty way of locking things up
> on my laptop every few minutes when the load is high enough to go into
> swap, while applying ck + inotify patches keep it running smoothly for
> me.  Actually, I use the archck patchset (these two plus a few more), as
> -cko doesnt seem to be maintained now.
> 
> Anyway, I did a "fakeroot make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image" after I
> patched stock 2.6.12 and did a make menuconfig, and the new kernel works
> just great.  I also installed newer versions of cpufreqd, laptop-mode
> -tools and the ipw2200 centrino wifi driver, (using debs available from
> their respective websites).
> 
> So now all I have to do is to tell apt-get not to try upgrading other
> kernels, or downgrading to antique and buggy versions of cpufreqd,
> laptop-mode and ipw2200 when I next do an apt-get upgrade.
> 
> Short question is - how do I mark certain packages as "don't touch
> these, I'll do it by hand" and still stay within debian's remarkably
> anal retentive packaging system?
> 
> 	srs

the state of just beginning to catch up with linux stuff. What i would
like to know is how they can develop thier linux knowledge and skills
to become atleast a novel user. If someone comes to you and wishes to
learn and become an efficient/skilled linuxian, what all would you
advice him to know.. better say what all you will ask him to learn and
practice ( step by step, ofcourse). Hope this reply would be useful to
all those passive members of the cominity who haven't yet come
forward, put questions and learn things.

without moving in for certifications! )

Hi 
On 9/15/05, Sudharshan S <sudharsh@gmail.com> wrote:
> hi amal,
> use this key combination ctrl+alt+f2, and ctrl+alt+f7 to exit

actually there's a minor problem in libvgahw.a (a library associated
with X) in FC4 and so the virtual consoles dont work properly in FC4.

The problem is discussed here and also a soln. is provided. In case u
have FC3 u can used this file from FC3.

http://fedoranews.org/mediawiki/index.php/Caveats_and_Known_Bugs_on_FC4

Jayakumar K K
From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Sep 15 07:10:20 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Sep 15 19:40:36 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Certification related discussion - Guide Beginners !
In-Reply-To: <73c0772405091506381a817203@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20050915141021.95749.qmail@web50203.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

My thoughts below,

--- Parth <parth.technofreak@gmail.com> wrote:
> like to know is how they can develop thier linux
> knowledge and skills
> to become atleast a novel user. 

It depends on what you want to use the system for and
what you want to learn.

GNU/Linux is an ocean.

a. There are some folks who might want to use
GNU/Linux as a desktop, and use it for their
day-to-day activities (office, printing, e-mail,
browsing, chat, etc.)

So, you will start of by working with different
software packages, distros, configuring them and using
them.

b. There are some who might want to go into
application development (distros, qt, gtk, scripting,
...)

How to become a hacker:
http://www.catb.org/~esr/faqs/hacker-howto.html

c. There are some who might want to go into operating
systems/hardware development (kernel, device drivers)

C and assembly language are a must. Starting off with
device drivers is good. For VLSI and embedded that are
GNU toolchains and free software available.

Check out this link from my domain:

http://www.shakthimaan.com -> Books

d. ...

So, you have to be very specific as to what your goals
are and what you want to learn and accomplish.

SK

Let me put it this way, I am just little less novice than the real noobs! 
When you try something in Linux (or even anything), you got into some 
problem, what would you do?

This is what I do and would do.

*) Try to fix it from with my current knowledge
*) If it seems to be distro specific, go to the distro site , look for 
solution.
*) Search community forum/list, if there's no existing post, post it there 
,as brief and as detailed as possible. Listing out things I have tried and 
the result of each. Try my best to show my enthusiam not frustration.
*) Yea.. google of course. 

Other DO's

Also,
*) Mistakes- Everyone does, learn from it. Don't repeat it.
*) The ancient ans of course:RTFM (many people did a good job of WTFM)
*) Read articles, webpages of the masters, ESR, Benjamin Mako Hill 
(Ubuntu/Debian),
Steve(Debian-administrations.com<http://Debian-administrations.com>),
to name a few.. and of course the masters in your own local lug. 
*) Back when I was in Trichy studying, used to collect second hand mags and 
hunt for article on Linux.
*) Meet some pal with similar interesting over a movie or beer in he 
weekends, you would occasionally find yourself getting to share lots of 
stuffs. (Thats how I got to know of putty when some dude mentioned it along 
ago).
*) Read certification exam guides , but don't go for certification ;-) , 
well actually, your choice. I really enjoyed reading Steve's RHCE guide, LPI 
guides on IBM Developerworks, and all articles by Daniel Robbins (Gentoo 
creator)
*) Yea.. also ESR's How to become a hacker
*) Help others when you can. 










-- 
benjamin rualthanzauva

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Sep 15 19:58:26 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Sep 15 20:32:25 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (DD)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509151907390.16498-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

The Free Software Foundations are proud to announce the creation of
the global "GPL Version 3 Development and Publicity Project". This 
activity is supported by no. of organizations. 
URL: http://www.gnu.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

dd -- Convert and copy a file.

Summary:

'dd' copies and optionally converts data with changeable I/O block
size. Reads are issued to the input file or device for the size of
the input buffer and writes are issued for the size of the output
buffer. This allows I/O requests to be tailored to the requirements of
a task. Output to standard error reports the number of full and short
blocks read and written.

Examples:

$ dd if=/dev/urandom of=ddfile bs=1 count=100 -- Dump random bytes in 
                                                 the file.

$ dd if=/dev/zero of=/dev/fd0 -- Format a floppy disk

$ dd if=/dev/fd0 of=/tmp/floppy.image -- Take floppy disk image.

$ echo "12345678901234567890" | dd bs=1 skip=5 count=10 -- Skip 5 
                          bytes in input and output only 10 Bytes.

$ echo "hello world" | dd cbs=1 conv=unblock -- Take one byte at a 
time and dump it in stdout with a new line.

$ echo "hello world" | dd conv=ucase -- Change to Upper case.

$ echo "HELLO WORLD" | dd conv=lcase -- Change to Lower case.

$ echo "12345678901234567890" > ddfile -- Dummy file.

$ echo "AAAAAAA" | dd bs=1 seek=5 of=ddfile count=5 conv=notrunc -- 
Seek 5 bytes in output file and copy only 5 from input to output file.

NOTE: You can use a some input file instead of echo command.

Read: man dd

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

DELHI PLANS AN AMBITIOUS FREEDEL MEET, WITH LOCAL CHAMBERS OF COMMERCE

Raj "Raju" Mathur <raju@linux-delhi.org> of ILUG-Delhi announces Freedel
to be held on September 17/18 2005, 10:00AM to 6:00PM at PHD House, Hauz
Khas, New Delhi. Two full days of demystifying [GNU]Linux. PHDCCI and
India Linux Users Group - Delhi (ILUG-D) are behind the event.

Says Mathur: "ILUG-D in the past has conducted very successful events
where over 450 participants attended. This year we are expecting much
greater numbers. People from all walks of life are expected to attend;
students, professionals, corporates, all will be there. What's more,
ILUG-D will have something to show for everyone. Technical talks
covering issues from installation, to desktop usage to wireless
[GNU]Linux, it will all be there. We will even have young school kids
showing how they use [GNU]Linux. Its an event you don't want to miss!"

Several stalls showcasing various aspects of Linux from gaming, to
audio/video editing to development, servers, databases and applications.

The event is organised by ILUG-D and co-hosted by PHD Chamber of
Commerce and Industry. It is completely volunteer-driven and supported
by several organisations. The event is primarily driven by volunteers
of ILUG-D and a committed group of computer professionals from PHDCCI.

Apart from all the technical stuff happening, there will also be
T-shirts, Linux distributions on CDs, tea, snacks and all the elements
of fun available at low or no cost.  Be there, be counted!

Contact: Raj Mathur raju@kandalaya.org  http://kandalaya.org/

[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]

THOSE FREE CDs IN YOUR HAND, THEY'RE ACTUALLY WORTH MILLIONS

Value of Debian GNU/Linux. The paper Measuring Libre Software
studying the size of the source packages in Debian 3.1 calculates the
size of sarge (close to 230 million lines of source code), the use of
the various programming languages in which the software has been
written, and the size of the packages included in the distribution. It
also estimates cost to create something on the scale of Debian from
scratch with a classical and well-known cost method (COCOMO) to be
over 8 billion US dollar.
http://www.upgrade-cepis.org/issues/2005/3/up6-3Amor.pdf
Source: Debian Weekly News http://www.debian.org/News/weekly/2005/37/

[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]o[</>]

dd if=/dev/hdb1 of=/dev/hdc1

is a collaborative forum for non-profit organisations,which brings NGOs,

platform for mutually beneficial relationships by helping, learning and 
sharing knowledge, resources and time. Non-profit organizations remain 
the central focus of CIOSA. As of now there are 120 NGOs 5 corporates  
and 43 individuals in our network.

We continuously try to built the capacities of our NGOs, as one of our 
efforts we would like to have a work-shop or seminar on Opensource for 
our members in the second week of October. In this we seek your 
assistance in developing content and organising the programme.

Our Members:

1.  CIOSA has member groups of varied causes.
  2.  From both urban and rural.
  3. 80% of them are small and medium sized
  4. Not many are computer savvy.
  5. Have problem with english.

What we Intend to achieve:

1. How opensource can help them in communication, and as alternate to 
mirosoft
2. Tamil search or interfaces.

These two may be different topic but we feel there is a need to teach 
our members how local languages can be used.

If this idea sounds good pl let us know how one can develop this and 
take it to many.

Subject: [Ilugc] BSNL DataOne Connection in RH9
In-Reply-To: <73c0772405091506254830c17c@mail.gmail.com>

hi,

> 
> 00.08.0  Ethernet Controler : RealTek Semiconductor Co., Ltd. RTL -
> 8139/8139c/8139c+ (rev 10)
> 

The above o/p shows that ur card uses one ethernet controller and the
driver for that is '8139too' .


> output of " /sbin/ifconfig -a "
> 
> lo      Link encap: Local Loopback
>        inet addr: 127.0.0.1  Mask: 255.0.0.0

ur eth0 is not activated.



> 
> insmod: /lib/modules/2.4.20-8/kernel/drivers/net/epic100.0:init_module:
> No such device
> insmod: Hint: insmod errors can be caused by incorrect module
> parameters, including
>                    invalid IO or IRQ parameters
> insmod: /lib/modules/2.4.20-8/kernel/drivers/net/epic100.0:init_module:
> insmod eth0 failed

the above statements prove that ur card has not been dtected properly.

Wht i suggest is
open the /etc/modules.conf
and delete all the entries in it relating to ethX and
then restart ur system. kudzu will generate some messages tht a card
has been removed and so. slect remove configuration but in the
following screen ( if u get one :)  )  choose ignore.

after that put one entry into the /etc/modules.conf file as follows,


alias  eth0 8139too

and i guess this shouls configure ur card correctly. ( alternatively
use redhat-config-network to  add the new card.)

tell me wht the results are.


regards,
kiran


1

On Friday 16 September 2005 13:56, kannan krishnamurthy wrote:
> Dear friends,
>
> I am using Redhat enterprise edition 3.0 in my office.
> can i have ghost image, what we used to take in
> windows. can any body help me???.
>
> Thanks and warm regards
>
> A. K.
>
> YOUR'S
>
> KANNAN.A.K.

You can probably do something using dd. Like this, for example:

dd if=/dev/hdXY of=hdXY.image bs=1024 count=716800

That copies 700 MB from /dev/hdXY (depending on the partition you need to 
image) to hdXY.image. To restore,

dd if=hdXY.image of=/dev/hdXY

I don't know how to span multiple discs with this technique, but someone else 
can probably help with that... :)

-- 
Shash

I did one such partition imaging. I tried dd and then partimage. I found 
partimage to be the best solution. I followed this tutorial:

http://freshmeat.net/articles/view/1375/

Do not use dd, it will copy each bit of data from the HDD. For 80GB HDD you 
will need big number of backup media.

hi,


> /dev/hdc1 - /boot - 200MB

u need not create a new boot partition. u can use the existing one.....



> I want to utilize the 10GB partition solely for RedHat 8.0,so that the
> above shown new hdd can be used for Ubuntu. Can I use dd command in the
> following way to to move the existing ubuntu system to new hdd ( don't
> want to install again).
> dd if=/dev/hdb1 of=/dev/hdc1
> dd if=/dev/hdb2 of=/dev/hdc2
> dd if=/dev/hdb3 of=/dev/hdc3

wht i suggest is instead of moving the existing ubuntu to the new hdd
let it stay in there.

create a new partion on the new hdd for redhat and in addition to that
u can create one more partion say 10GB on the new hdd mount it on
/misc and then cp all the files in /usr to misc
and then unmount it. Then u can edit the /etc/fstab at mount the new
partition as /usr on the existing ubuntu. Since the size of /usr is
increased u can get very vast amount of root storages space at the
same time u can delete the contents of /usr from the original dir (
caution lest u delete files from the new partion after u mount it)




> Will it work? Can I run these command while while the system is running
> on Ubuntu runlevel 1? or I have to do these when I run Redhat system?
> I have installed GRUB in MBR of /dev/hdb. Apart from editing the
> /boot/grub/menu.lst file, what else I have to do?


i guess the above thing should work, but no idea.  If u r trying it
tell us about the results.

On 9/18/05, baluk <baluk54@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> After doing an update of fc4 i find that fc4 does not boot properly.the
> display goes haywire and only blotches of colors appear on the monitor.
> 
> 
It's a well-known problem in libvgahw.a of FC4. Just replace it with
libvgahw.a from FC3, and you should be OK. The better fix is to
recompile xorg-x11 from SRPM using gcc-4.0.1, but that requires
a working FC4 or FC3 box, and it's more work than most people
are willing to do.

-Siva

From manokaran at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 13:08:15 2005
From: manokaran at gmail.com (Mano)
Date: Mon Sep 19 13:08:24 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...
Message-ID: <7bf1bec5050919003852bdfb3e@mail.gmail.com>

http://www.bcs.org/BCS/Products/publishing/itnow/OnlineArchive/sep05/itnowextra/memberview.htm

The abv is a link to an article that discusses some of the problems
with OSS. Personally, I feel there is some truth when the author says:

"The open source community has so far tended to create facsimiles of
proprietary packages rather than the next killer application.  Linux
is an excellent example. Although it contains many powerful new tools
and utilities, Linux is in essence a facsimile of Unix, a proprietary
operating system first developed at Bell Telephone Laboratories in
1969. Ironically, the legendary robustness of Linux actually owes more
to the good design of Unix and its older relative, Multics, than it
does the OSS development process."

Will OSS be able to deliver an app that defines and creates its own
market - something like what Photoshop or Dreamweaver or Lotus Notes
did in their respective domains? Will OSS be able to deliver that tool
that will mark a paradigm shift in the way people use their computers?

regds,
mano

On 9/19/05, Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com> wrote:
 
> The reviews on slashdot.org:
> 
> http://developers.slashdot.org/article.pl?sid=05/09/18/1549249&tid=185&tid=8

Let us have a mind of our own and review it ourselves!

> "Intellectual Property" is a very biased term misused
> by corporate for their selfish needs.
> 
> Check the presentation on "Danger of Software Patents
> by Richard Stallman":

The question here is: will OSS deliver an earthshaking app. 

My take:
OSS enthusiasts revel in solving programming challenges rather than
solving real world problems (I use the word 'real' to mean problems in
the application space). So they choose a programming task that already
solved a 'real' world problem (say Unix) and reimplement it in a more
elegant and bug free manner (linux). All the adrenaline one craves for
is generated by this deed itself. But the fact remains that it is only
a 'reimplementation' of a solution conceptualized by someone else.

more later.

regds,
mano

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 17:21:15 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Sep 19 17:21:27 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...
In-Reply-To: <7bf1bec5050919003852bdfb3e@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7bf1bec5050919003852bdfb3e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f99012050919045144fe34ec@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/19/05, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> 
> http://www.bcs.org/BCS/Products/publishing/itnow/OnlineArchive/sep05/itnowextra/memberview.htm
> 
> The abv is a link to an article that discusses some of the problems
> with OSS. Personally, I feel there is some truth when the author says:
> 
> "The open source community has so far tended to create facsimiles of
> proprietary packages rather than the next killer application. Linux
> is an excellent example. Although it contains many powerful new tools
> and utilities, Linux is in essence a facsimile of Unix, a proprietary
> operating system first developed at Bell Telephone Laboratories in
> 1969. Ironically, the legendary robustness of Linux actually owes more
> to the good design of Unix and its older relative, Multics, than it
> does the OSS development process."


This is a myth which keeps getting repeated again and again, and like
all myths, starts with a small kernel of truth. In this case, that kernel 
relates
to the Linux kernel, which was originally written to work in a manner
similar to the Unix kernel as described in various textbooks, including
books by Bach and Tanenbaum that were widely in use at that time.
It definitely is not a facsimile copy of Unix - there is no source code 
that is common between the Linux kernel and the Unix kernel.

OTOH, the GNU userland that is commonly used in conjunction with
the Linux kernel to form the GNU/Linux OS, was originally written to
be a replacement for the userland(s) that shipped with commercial
implementations of Unix. There should be no surprise that it broadly
implements the same functionality - because that is what it was written
to do. Again, there is no common source code between the GNU
utilities and the Unix utilities, so neither is the copy of the other.

The ideas that inspired Unix definitely had a root in the Multics
project, but the implementation did not. Likewise, the ideas that
inspired GNU/Linux had a root in Unix, but not the implementation.

-Siva
From manokaran at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 17:23:04 2005
From: manokaran at gmail.com (Mano)
Date: Mon Sep 19 17:23:16 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] url redirection without url change
In-Reply-To: <20050919114350.78107.qmail@web31807.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <20050919114350.78107.qmail@web31807.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <7bf1bec505091904537ef9f549@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/19/05, saravanan ganapathy <sarav_gsa@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hai ,
> 
> I would like to redirect a url ( http://my.url1.com)
> to another url ( http://www.url1.com/abc/) without
> changing the url in the browser.

If you want the file 'abc' to be displayed when a user types
my.url1.com then you specify 'abc' as the default file to be sent in
your web server config file.

If you want the browser to know only my.url1.com and not www.url1.com
but still get 'abc' from www.url1.com then you should make my.url1.com
a proxy client - a simple script that just posts the request to the
new server, gets back the html file and just pass it on to the
browser!

Hope this helps.

mano

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 17:33:42 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)

	<fa9c0711050919015965b87f1d@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/19/05, Chakkaradeep C.C. <chakkaradeepcc@gmail.com> wrote:

> 
> what made me to think is about the issues related to OSS and
> mainly,*Intellectual
> Property.*It is true that if you are not seld-employed,then whatever you
> discover belongs to the private organization if at all you use their
> resources.


Not true at all - the term Intellectual Property is misleading, and attempts
to use a single term to describe a number of widely differing legal 
principles
with vastly different rules. They are:

1) Patent Law
2) Copyright Law
3) Trademarks
4) Trade Secrets
5) Law of Contracts

Whatever you discover doesn't belong to the organization that employs you -
that is governed by Patent Law and the Law of Contracts. In particular, your
ideas don't belong to your employer by default unless you assign them to
your employer.

> a) is there a common Package Management System available?


Why should there be one? If you don't like any particular one, you are
free to stop using it or write your own.

b) if somebody asks you help on using linux,which linux distribution will u
> choose among all available!


The one that help was sought about, naturally.

c) the appln which i develop today, can it be installed after 1 year in an
> linux distro?


It is *your responsibility* to ensure that your app. will work with distros 
and
other apps in the future. If you write it according certain general 
guidelines and
principles, it should work for the conceivable future with any distro.

-Siva
From zenmurugan at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 17:41:52 2005
From: zenmurugan at gmail.com (Senthil Murugan)
Date: Mon Sep 19 17:42:10 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] url redirection without url change 
References: <20050919114350.78107.qmail@web31807.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <03b901c5bd13$5749a680$270110ac@sevco>

> I would like to redirect a url ( http://my.url1.com)
> to another url ( http://www.url1.com/abc/) without
> changing the url in the browser.

In your my.url1.com web server configuration file(httpd.conf) , I guess you 
will be having the virtual host

------------
<VirtualHost XXX.XXX.XXX.XXX >
    ServerName my.url1.com
    Redirect permanent /  http://www.url1.com/abc/
    .....
</VirtualHost>
------------------
where  XXX.XXX.XXX.XXX is the ip address of the my.url1.com

Thanks,
SenthilMurugan

If the problem had actually been solved earlier to perfection, there
would have been no need to reinvent the wheel. The very fact that
the wheel was reinvented shows that the earlier solution was incomplete
or imperfect. 

I definitely do *not* want to replace my copy of Linux-2.6.13 with Unix
System 7 or whatever - that is not a *solution* to my *problem*.

Finding and solving problems is entirely orthogonal to the OSS
methodology, but as a matter of practical fact, OSS addresses this
much better than closed development efforts. Take a look at the
Beowulf project (for Linux clustering) or the Xen project (for para-
virtualization) - there's no equivalent in the closed-source world.
There are numerous other examples, but these two came to mind
immediately.

-Siva

> earlier. Is it capable of finding and solving problems on its own!

Well, let's take it a step further then ... Microsoft has been trying to 
implement an OS -- which is a problem that has been solved earlier. I 
mean, just because a piece of software falls in a class which contains 
other programs written already (be it unix-like OSes or OSes in general), 
are you saying, any further work on it is useless ?

Linux was like unix only in it's interface to applications and users - the 
fact that it was a reimplementation implies that he redid the whole thing 
.. and lots of people think he did a better job at it than traditional 
unix. Linux now runs on far more platforms than unix does. Since 2.6, it's 
multitasking has been a lot-better as well. It supports a lot of devices 
and peripherals .. if all this doesn't seem like "Solving a new problem" 
to you, well ... !

And if you want to see Free Software that solves "new" problems, think of 
programs like jabberd (and please don't say IM is solved .. jabber allows 
linking to other non-jabber networks), bitlbee, emacs (i mean, emacs 
fanatics will tell you there is no problem, new or old, that emacs can't 
solve), BitTorrent, etc.

--ayan

From zenmurugan at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 19:44:14 2005
From: zenmurugan at gmail.com (Senthil Murugan)
Date: Mon Sep 19 19:44:32 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] url redirection without url change 
Message-ID: <03f801c5bd24$6d8d3450$270110ac@sevco>

> I would like to redirect a url ( http://my.url1.com)
> to another url ( http://www.url1.com/abc/) without
> changing the url in the browser.

In your my.url1.com web server configuration file(httpd.conf) , I guess you
will be having the virtual host

------------
<VirtualHost XXX.XXX.XXX.XXX >
    ServerName my.url1.com
    Redirect permanent /  http://www.url1.com/abc/
    .....
</VirtualHost>
------------------
where  XXX.XXX.XXX.XXX is the ip address of the my.url1.com

Thanks,
SenthilMurugan

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Sep 19 20:13:20 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Sep 19 20:10:59 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (TIME)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509191922260.25034-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Open Source Technology Group (OSTG) is the leading network of
technology sites provide unbiased contents(news, articles...),
community, and commerce for the Linux & Open Source communities. 
URL: http://www.ostg.com/

One Day One Command 
===================

time -- Measure the program resource usage

Summary:

The `time' command runs another program, then displays information
about the resources used by that program, collected by the system
while the program was running.

Info consist of (i) Elapsed real time between invocation and
termination, (ii) User CPU time and (iii) System CPU time.

Examples:

$ time ls -- Run the ls and show usage info.

$ time -p ls -- Same above. Output in portable format.

# time -o file ls -- Redirect the output to a file.

# time -a -o file ls -- Append the output to a file.

# time -v sleep 6 -- Show more detail info.

# time -f "\t%E real,\t%U user,\t%S sys" sleep 6 -- Show formatted 
                                                    output.

Note: By using custom output format, we can print (I) Time,
(II) Memory and (III) I/O Resource informations.

Read: man time

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/
