saravanan ganapathy wrote: 
,----
| We can  redirect the  url using mod_rewrite,  but this 'll  change the
| url.
`----

Its not *redirect*. Its *rewrite*.  mod_rewrite is nifty. You could do
something like this:

http://puggy.symonds.net/~suraj/ragas/priya

and to get this done, I have the following in my .htaccess:

RewriteRule ragas/(.*)$ karnatik_ragasearch.php?raga=$1 [L]

In effect, whatever follows ragas/(.*) gets sent to the underlying PHP
app. and thats *without* redirection.

Please read up more about mod_rewrite.

cheers,

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Mon Sep 19 23:20:58 2005

>  Thats exactly the point - OSS solves a problem which has been solved
> earlier. Is it capable of finding and solving problems on its own!

One point which I feel is being missed is that it is the quality of
the implementations that sets apart applications, be it FOSS or
proprietary. Application ideas come out first, independent of whether
the implementation is free or otherwise. Like quoted previously, an OS
was an idea, picture filters was an idea, etc. For an OS, a have a
free alternative (Linux) and other non-free ones. Similarly, Gimp vs
PhotoShop. What I think gives FOSS its credibility is how well these
implementations are done. Be it mplayer for playing video, or tidy for
cleaning up HTML; what makes FOSS great is how complete these
implementations are. One can say with much confidence that it would be
a really tough task to find an app with more features for playing
video than mplayer, or with more features for optimizing HTML than
tidy. I would say that FOSS has succeeded in delivering such products
in many application areas.

it moves on...

for what they are, the signs of our ideas, and not for things themselves.
                                     -John Locke, philosopher (1632-1704)

If a man will begin with certainties, he shall end in doubts; but if
he will be content to begin with doubts, he shall end in certainties.
-Francis Bacon

Within quotes are statements made by others. My response to them follow :-

"If the problem had actually been solved earlier to perfection, there
would have been no need to reinvent the wheel. The very fact that
the wheel was reinvented shows that the earlier solution was incomplete
or imperfect."

No problem can be solved to perfection. If linux 2.6.13 solves the os
problem perfectly we wont need 2.7 or 2.8! The point that am making is
that the wheel has been invented and OSS only polishes the wheel. The
question I do not know an answer for is: can OSS 'invent' the wheel?

"  I definitely do *not* want to replace my copy of Linux-2.6.13 with Unix
System 7 or whatever  - that is not a *solution* to my *problem*. "

Unix System 7 was intended to solve a problem of its times. If one can
travel back in time, say to late 70s, and offer to replace Unix with
linux-2.6.13 am sure there will be no takers. Who will need support
for WiFi  or, say, firefox in 1970?

"Take a look at the Beowulf project (for Linux clustering) or the Xen
project (for para-
virtualization) - there's no equivalent in the closed-source world."

Am not knowledgeable enough to comment on Beowulf. Nor Xen ... but is
not Xen solving a problem (albeit differently) that VMWare already
does?

"I mean, just because a piece of software falls in a class which contains
other programs written already (be it unix-like OSes or OSes in general),
are you saying, any further work on it is useless ?"

I never said that!

> and I guess all the little  innovations that make up emacs and vim end
> up being  'cannibalised' by  other non-free software.   fetchmail, who
> beats? and what  about screen?  Isn't that really  an innovation? Auto
> completion is definitely a cute innovation, IMO.

'cute' innovations are not the issue here.

Most responses highlight the incremental innovation being added by the
FOSS model of s/w dev. I do  not deny this at all. My question is
still unanswered: Can OSS give an application that is mutative... not
incremental.

regds,
mano

From vijairaj.r at gmail.com  Tue Sep 20 10:16:13 2005

Subject: [Ilugc] Ghost image
In-Reply-To: <20050916082606.10487.qmail@web31913.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <20050916082606.10487.qmail@web31913.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <5d0d0e3105092001161106f1ea@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/16/05, kannan krishnamurthy <kannan_6074@yahoo.com> wrote:
> 
> Dear friends,
> 
> I am using Redhat enterprise edition 3.0 in my office.
> can i have ghost image, what we used to take in
> windows. can any body help me???.
> 

Just a backup of the individual partions you use will be enough.

To make the backup you need or have to know certain things.
1. An alternate linux installation/live cd.
2. If you dont have any of the above then you can prepare a ramdisk with the 
required filesystem modules and boot with the ramdisk as the root 
filesystem.
3. You have to know what all the partitions are required to be backed up. 
The entire filesystem tree can reside on a single partitions or on multiple 
partions(typically these other partitions are mounted on /usr, /var, 
/boot... ). 
4. Once you have figured out the partitions, just mount it somewhere and 
make a zipped tar image of the folder.
5. Take care to preserver the permission and attributes while backingup.
6. While restoring, you should check the fstab file and make the required 
changes.
7. Rest is left for you to research.

--
Vijairaj

If the entire file system tree is on a single partition, it is very simple.

From babu_jayapaul at yahoo.com  Tue Sep 20 02:44:28 2005
From: babu_jayapaul at yahoo.com (babu jayapaul)
Date: Tue Sep 20 15:14:43 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] url redirection without url change 
In-Reply-To: <20050919114350.78107.qmail@web31807.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20050920094428.30467.qmail@web31013.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

Hi,

You can change in 3 ways, if you are using apache

1) "Using a Perl script with Virtual Host" 

<VirtualHost 61.247.252.103>
ServerAdmin linuz@globalanalytics.com
ServerName www.global-analytics.com
DocumentRoot /www/htdocs/

ScriptAlias /mark/articles "/www2/CAS.pl"
</VirtualHost>

The ScriptAlias is the key part here. It redirects all
requests from /mark/articles to the CAS.pl perl
script.

And the perl script looked like this,

#!/usr/bin/perl


print "Location:
http://www.globalanalytics.com$ENV{'REQUEST_URI'}";

$ENV{'REQUEST_URI'} is the key part here.

---------------------------------------------------
2) Using the mod_rewrite module for Apache

I compiled mod_rewrite into Apache and applied this
configuration option to httpd.conf.

<VirtualHost 61.247.252.103>
ServerAdmin linuz@globalanalytics.com
ServerName www.global-analytics.com
DocumentRoot /www/htdocs/

RewriteEngine on
RewriteCond %{HTTP_HOST} 
^www\.global\-analytics\.com$
#RewriteRule ^(/articles)(.*)
http://www.globalanalytics.com/
</VirtualHost>

------------------------------------------------
3) Using Redirect with Virtual Host -- "Simple method"

<VirtualHost 61.247.252.103>
ServerAdmin linuz@globalanalytics.com
ServerName www.global-analytics.com
DocumentRoot /www/htdocs/

Redirect /gas/ http://www.globalanalytics.com/
</VirtualHost>

--------------------------------

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Sep 20 19:56:18 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Sep 20 19:53:26 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (GCC)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509201906580.1534-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Linux From Scratch (LFS) is a project that provides you with 
step-by-step instructions for building your own GNU/Linux OS 
from source code. URL: http://www.linuxfromscratch.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

gcc -- GNU C Compiler

Summary:

Several versions of the compiler (C, C++, Objective-C, Ada, Fortran,
and Java) are integrated; this is why we use the name "GNU Compiler
Collection". GCC can compile programs written in any of these above
languages.

This C program is used in the examples.

#define DISPLAY "Hello World\n"
main()
{
 #ifdef MACRO
    printf(DISPLAY);
 #else
    printf("No Macro\n");
 #endif
}

Examples:

$ gcc hello.c -- Place output in a.out file.

$ ./a.out -- Run the binary file.

$ gcc -Wall hello.c -- Show all warning messages.

$ gcc -c hello.c -- Compile, Don't Link. Place output in hello.o

$ gcc -S hello.c -- Stop after the stage of compilation proper 
                    and save the ASM code in hello.s file.

$ gcc -DMACRO hello.c -- Predefine a Macro.

$ gcc -E hello.c -- Stop after the preprocessing stage and print 
                    output in stdout.

$ gcc hello.c -o hello -- Place output in hello file.

$ ./hello -- Run the binary file.

$ gcc -v hello.c -o hello -- Show the details of compilation stages.

$ gcc -I./myIncludes/ hello.c -- In myIncludes Dir also search for
                                 the Header files.

Read: man or info gcc

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

On 9/21/05, Partho Protim Paul <penguin.partho@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> rpm's are a bit messy. i would suggest u to compile from source. 
> it takes a very long time. so please be patient. and then after that run 
> # xorgcfg -textmode
> 

Building and installing from tarballs on an RPM-based distro is invariably
bad practice, and will definitely cause maintenance problems down the road.
Don't even dream of trying it on XFree86/Xorg - the downstream dependencies
are humongous.

Stick with the SRPMs. That way, if you have a bad build or need to downgrade
or upgrade the RPMs for any reason, it's a breeze.

-Siva

On 9/21/05, Partho Protim Paul <penguin.partho@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> i dont think building from source is a bad practice at all.


You don't get the point at all. Building from SRPMs and building from a 
source
tarball are both similar, in that they involve building from source. 
However, when
you build from SRPM, you obtain RPMs that can be 
installed/de-installed/upgraded/
down-graded/..., using the package manager (rpm), which tracks all upstream 
and
downstream dependencies. That's a *huge* advantage over building from a 
plain
source tarball. 

(Yes, I know that you can also perform rpmbuild from tarball, but that 
requires a
specfile and is not very different from building from SRPM).

i did build my xorg from bz2 tar ball and i dont have a single problem, may 
> be thats gods grace. 


Anybody can build an xorg or anything else for that matter from a tarball. 
But can you
de-install, upgrade or downgrade it cleanly, while ensuring that *all* 
dependencies are
satisfied?

posix is based on building from source. 


Huh? Posix is a collection of standards, not a package.

and srpms are also sources dude, dont you agree?? u can virtually control 
> all the process ur going to perform through source code or sprms. but plain 
> old rpms are for newcomers... too bad i used to come to that ring before, 
> but i guess i am now mature enough to run the process of upgrading 
> applications through source be it BSD or Linux. 


Maybe you need to switch to Gentoo. Make sure you check out the Gentoo-Ricer
comparison at http://funroll-loops.org/

On 9/20/05, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:

> The point that am making is
> that the wheel has been invented and OSS only polishes the wheel. The
> question I do not know an answer for is: can OSS 'invent' the wheel?

There is no such thing as "OSS" (Open Source Software), because Open
Source is only a marketing program for Free Software and one would not
expect them  to invent new things.  Free Software is the wheel here,
and we could give full marks to OSI for polishing the wheel well and
setting it rolling.

If we take Free Software, GNU operating system with HURD aims for an
os with no limits, which I think is original[1].

The most important innovation is that the freedom in the Free Software
environment makes Artificial Intelligence and Artificial Life
*theoretically* possible.  If a set of programs ever evolve to the
point of substantially improving themselves, Free Software environment
allows them regenerate giving birth to legitimate new versions,
whereas in a non-free software environment, the process will simply
abort. Machines could then think without getting emotional -
particularly about the fate of programmers who will then lose their
jobs and livelihood ;)

-Ramanraj K

[1] http://kilobug.free.fr/hurd/pres-en/abstract/html/node4.html

You are right. Initially I decided to use GNU Compiler Collection in
that place. But I thought, It may confuse the newbie. So I used simple
term in that place and I added a extra info in the Summary section.

> > Several versions of the compiler (C, C++, Objective-C, Ada, Fortran,

proceed. unless u have fiddled with it. i did ask and paste the whole log of 
the installation to #gcc in irc://irc.oftc.org and they said thats a bug and 
they are examining the entire process. and its not just me many have 
reported the same problem. they looked at the make bootstrap code and said 
it in public in the #gcc channel ( this is the official gcc developers 
channel on irc) that its buggy and they are going to roll back. and not 
release any pre-release till all the bugs are fixed. 
even i am using gcc 4.0.0 on my openBSD 3.7 machine. 
$ /usr/local/bin/egcc -v
Using built-in specs.
Target: i386-unknown-openbsd3.7
Configured with:

--verbose --program-transform-name=s,^,e, --disable-nls --disable-checking

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Thu Sep 22 07:11:08 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Thu Sep 22 07:11:17 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...
In-Reply-To: <43315E3B.90400@gmail.com>
References: <43315E3B.90400@gmail.com>

On 9/21/05, Sudharshan S <sudharsh@gmail.com> wrote:

> >The most important innovation is that the freedom in the Free Software
> >environment makes Artificial Intelligence and Artificial Life
> >*theoretically* possible.  If a set of programs ever evolve to the
> >point of substantially improving themselves, Free Software environment
> >allows them regenerate giving birth to legitimate new versions,
> >
> hmmm. reminds me of steven spielberg's flick AI.

It would be better if it reminds us of our own ancient philosophy that
devised the number place system and countless other innovations that
allow intelligence to express itself ;)

> evolution of softwares
> by themselves seems to be a gr8 idea,

The tools for doing that are already there. One could compile emacs
with emacs, gcc with gcc and probably others with far less
sophistication.  AFAIK, we are just one step away from letting
software evolve by itself:  we do not take sufficient care to define
functions more carefully and elaborately - once that is done, programs
would be able to see what we are after, and may be help us there.

> but think of it. it invites
> mischief, even then these *intelligent* softwares must follow a protocol
> of some sort,

That "protocol of some sort" has been around for a long time, and it
is known as Law.  How would a robot know it is not "proper" to hit
another person: If it has some idea about the Indian Penal Code, there
is a good chance it may reason that its master would become liable for
its acts, and may avoid hitting others.

> and not just give *birth* to newer versions, u'll hav a
> population explosion

Patches would be sent to the central repository as usual, where humans
or robots may evaluate the patch, and any "population explosion" could
be controlled.

Already, Free Software may be modified and redistributed, but we see
that when we talk of "emacs", by default it means a emacs version
released by FSF. Others like debian may have made modifications to
just suit its own environment or new branches like XEmacs may evolve.
But ultimately user preferences keep the population explosion in check
and control.

> and a whole new dimension of virtual world will be
> created and the line between reality and virtuality will disappear, ever
> seen 'Ghost in the Shell: Stand alone complex' on 'animax', something
> like that.

Ever read Sankaracarya's Daksinamurti Stotra that begins with about
"having understood that the world is within oneself even as a city
reflected in a mirror is, but projected as if it is outside, by maya,
as in dream"[1].  It was shocking when I realised what it really
meant.

We just have to check for truth as usual ;)  Already, some programs
allow us to "update" applications "automatically".  Would you not
check something for bugs or features before "updating" ?  It is nice
to have things done "automatically", but you still need to check with
your own senses before you start using anything new. If we ever *stop*
doing that, there is a grave danger thereafter.

> and even if *emotional* softwares comes into existence i bet it will be
> from the open source world and not from some lame M****$**t

Did you reason why?  Calling something lame without reason is unfair.

We could compile emacs with emacs or gcc with gcc because we have the
source, and further the GPL allows you to to do it - in fact you are
encouraged to do such naughty things and contribute patches ;)  You
cannot complile VC++ , or whatever non-free software,  because it does
not come with source code and further even if it does come, its
licence would prevent you from compiling new versions and
redistributing it.  We could say: Free software has life but non-free
software is sterile.

- Ramanraj K

The spirited mind will not be content to remain within itself - it
will reach out for chances to prove its worth. (- Heard somewhere)
From sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in  Thu Sep 22 10:15:08 2005
From: sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in (Prof. P. Sriram)
Date: Thu Sep 22 10:15:10 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] List Admin
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509211425230.3575-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509211425230.3575-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0509221006420.31863@gateway.ae.iitm.ac.in>

i (through bharathi) have received 4 names for possible list admins. what
work does being list admin involve? typically, 5-10 minutes a day with a
browser is all it takes. list admin needs to 'moderate' non-member posts
to the list and also occasionally clear the list of defunct members (those
who dont bother to sign off the list, but leave a dead email address
subscribed). we get maybe a half a dozen spam mails directed to the list
every day - these are held over for list admin to deal with. every so
often, a legit list member tries to post from a non-subscribed email
address and this too gets held over for list admin. we also get replies to
multi-list cross postings and these may be of interest to the list. list
admin gets email periodically when such posts are held over. list admin
just needs to login through the list admin web interface and make a few
strategic clicks to junk/approve the pending non-member posts (default is
junk). some actions cant be done from the web interface (will need shell 
access) and i will take care of these as and when i am alerted. so, being 
list admin is quite easy, no?

-- 
sriram

On 9/21/05, Ramanraj K <ramanraj.k@gmail.com> wrote:
> There is no such thing as "OSS" (Open Source Software), because Open
> Source is only a marketing program for Free Software and one would not
> expect them  to invent new things.  Free Software is the wheel here,
> and we could give full marks to OSI for polishing the wheel well and
> setting it rolling.

I do agree that the FSS movement did shake the earth about how s/w is
developed. But this is not my question. Perhaps I was not clear when I
asked if OSS will invent the wheel. I did not mean OSS as a s/w
development model. I meant it as a business model. Let me rephrase my
question:

A software company does not patent any of its innovations (cute ones
included) and releases all its code to the general community. If the
innovation is of value there will be dozens of other companies that
seek to provide support for the same s/w undercutting prices to a
level that throws the original company out of business (if it is not
properly managed). After a period the market will only have highly
efficient players who can account for the productivity of every penny.

Now, the question is: Can these super efficient players afford sinking
money in research projects that might (just might) give them the next
killer app. Since developing a killer app is unpredictable, can these
companies stay in business till their research team comes out with the
'killer'? Can these companies do a Bell and employ the likes of Ken
Thompson, Dennis Ritchi, Kernighan, Pike etc and not care for 5 years
or so about what value they have added to their revenues? Would not
the other efficient players wipe such a company out of the market in a
year? How will the free thinking of great minds be funded? And even if
such a company gives out such a product will it have sufficient time
to recoup investments before the others catch up (the others can be
super efficient because they did not spend a penny on research and
have got the source code for free)?

> If we take Free Software, GNU operating system with HURD aims for an
> os with no limits, which I think is original[1].

HURD follows the microkernel approach but for all its advantages it is
still a fringe player.

> The most important innovation is that the freedom in the Free Software
> environment makes Artificial Intelligence and Artificial Life
> *theoretically* possible.  If a set of programs ever evolve to the
> point of substantially improving themselves, Free Software environment
> allows them regenerate giving birth to legitimate new versions,
> whereas in a non-free software environment, the process will simply
> abort. Machines could then think without getting emotional -
> particularly about the fate of programmers who will then lose their
> jobs and livelihood ;)

Interesting but not relevant to this thread :-) Will contribute to
this in a different thread.

mano
-
All those who believe in psychokinesis, raise my hand.

--- Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> A software company does not patent any of its
> innovations (cute ones
> included) and releases all its code to the general
> community. If the
> innovation is of value there will be dozens of other
> companies that
> seek to provide support for the same s/w
> undercutting prices to a
> level that throws the original company out of
> business (if it is not
> properly managed). 

Software is complex. It is not easy for every Jack and
Jill to understand code. You will have millions and
millions of lines of inter-dependant code.

When you have software code, software professionals
build on the code, or use only a module of the entire
release code and develop more projects on them.

> After a period the market will
> only have highly
> efficient players who can account for the
> productivity of every penny.

Yes. Value is given to real products. Companies who do
workarounds in their products and try to sell things
without bug fixes cannot survive. The customer gets a
proper product for the money he spends on it, compared
to proprietary closed-source models, where you pay for
stuff which you are not sure if it really does what it
is supposed to do. A name rings a bell in my mind!

> Now, the question is: Can these super efficient
> players afford sinking
> money in research projects that might (just might)
> give them the next
> killer app. 

Dude, there are lot of companies in India who already
do R&D using GNU/Linux in embedded systems/VLSI. Check
my database collection:

http://www.shakthimaan.com -> Database

> Can these companies do a Bell and employ
> the likes of Ken
> Thompson, Dennis Ritchi, Kernighan, Pike etc and not
> care for 5 years
> or so about what value they have added to their
> revenues? 

R&D can also be for a year or two. 

Yes, we make money out of it.

> Would not
> the other efficient players wipe such a company out
> of the market in a
> year? 

Nope. 

ARM have their headquarters in UK. Russell King works
for Deep Blue Solutions and works on ARM Linux
development. CodeSourcery Inc have done the compiler
toolchain build using GNU for ARM. Don't tell me they
are out of the market. ARM rules the embedded world.

> How will the free thinking of great minds be
> funded? 

Software is not a manufacturing industry. Because of
its nature, it falls into a service industry, where,
companies earn income through maintenance and tech
support.

Are you a business person? or a technical guy? If you
don't mind, can you tell in which domain you work on?

> HURD follows the microkernel approach but for all
> its advantages it is
> still a fringe player.

In the industry, yes. In the academia, no.

L4ka::pistachio microkernel was developed in
University of Karlsruhe, Germany.  Hurd is being
ported to it:

http://www.gnu.org/software/hurd/hurd-l4.html

http://www.l4ka.org/projects/pistachio/

Work is going on.

From ee01b098 at ee.iitm.ac.in  Thu Sep 22 16:08:44 2005
From: ee01b098 at ee.iitm.ac.in (Ayan Chakrabarti)
Date: Thu Sep 22 16:08:58 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...
In-Reply-To: <7bf1bec50509220310490a2ef0@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509221543460.17118-100000@athreya.ee.iitm.ernet.in>

> How will giving jack and jill (customers) source code make a
> difference. They anyway will not know if it really does what it says
> it does?

This is the whole point of "Free Software". Jack and Jill's right to get 
the source code for the software they buy. Its not about giving away 
software for free, nor is it about bringing down microsoft, or the 
philosophical intricacies of reinventing/polishing/'making a square' 
wheel. Open Source is about the collaborative benefits of freely available 
source, Free Software is about the fact that when I buy software from you, 
I WANT and have a right to the source code.

I've added custom patches to dozens of programs currently running on my 
system - right from scilab to gaim to aterm to my window manager, and I 
don't know how I'd get any work done without them.  It doesn't matter 
whether I'm in an overwhelming minority, I still have a right to this 
freedom. It's not about whether it makes sense for the company to do so 
.. it's a consumer right ! The Free Software movement, unlike the Open 
source one, is about what's best for the user, not what's the best 
development / money minting model. So, while Open Source supports may be 
amenable to "special exceptions" to the give the source with the software 
rule, we're not !

People will always be around to give reasons why such a freedom will spell 
doom for the industry. I mean, you can always find reasons why x will 
spell doom for y, for every ordered pair (x,y). That's not the point. The 
point is, if enough *users* are educated about the benefits of having the 
source code of the software, and then go ahead and demand it from 
software vendors, I'm sure every company will be forced to find a way to 
foster innovation AND give the user the source.

--Ayan
$$\lim_{\mbox[CGPA] \to 0}engineer = manager$$

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Sep 22 20:53:54 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Sep 22 20:50:42 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (LTRACE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509222021100.19405-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Linux From Scratch (LFS) is a project that provides you with 
step-by-step instructions for building your own GNU/Linux OS 
from source code. URL: http://www.linuxfromscratch.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

ltrace -- Library call TRACEr

Summary:

ltrace is a program that simply runs the specified command until it
exits and intercepts & records the library/system calls, which are
called by the executed process, and the signals, which are received by
that process. It can used study the internal flow of a program.

Examples:

$ ltrace sleep 1 -- Trace all Lib call of 'sleep' command.

$ ltrace ls -- Trace all Lib call of 'ls' command.

$ ltrace -d sleep 1 -- Print more detailed info.

$ ltrace -i sleep 1 -- Print the value of the Instruction Pointer at 
                       every lib call.

$ ltrace -S sleep 1 -- Show System Call trace also.

$ ltrace -S -L sleep 1 -- Show only System calls.

$ ltrace -r sleep 1 -- Print a relative time-stamp with each line of
                       the trace.

$ ltrace -t sleep 1 -- Prefix each line of the trace with the time of
                       day.

$ ltrace -o file sleep 1 -- Redirect the output to a file.

$ sleep 60 & -- Dummy background Job.

$ ltrace -p 1234 -- Attach to the process with the PID 1234 (use dummy 
                    job's Pid) and trace.

$ ltrace -n 3 sleep 1 -- Indent each new nested call by 3 Spaces.

Read: man ltrace

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

> right?
It is a fundamental right because it has controlling function like
government. Do not treat software like product, think it like
government. Its role is seen in our life, not just as system
personnel, as end user also. e.g. from bank-to-diagnosis-to-electing
prime ministers. Software interfers in our personal life. Have you
ever seen a car taking you to automatically to a red-light area
without your consent, but a software browser takes me to a such sites
without consent. Well that is the power of software - it has
controlling and governing function. That is why software requires
some public control.

Coming to your coke analogy, do you know that all food items are
governed by PFA-Prevention of Food Adulration act, which empowers
government agencies to check the content and take leagal action in
case it is not fit for human consumption.  Can government do this say
for example examining a closed source software which takes you to
illegal site? Does any such agency exists? As long as there is no
other public auditing mechanism like PFA established  the only viable
option left is access to source code to ensure our personal freedom.

Do not look software purely as science/technlogy/business. It has
social and personal angle also.

This is just to provoke thoughtful emotion.

Raman.P

Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...

References: <7bf1bec50509220310490a2ef0@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/23/05, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> But what makes this a
> fundamental right? One doesnt ask for Coke's formula when one buys
> Coke. Or ask for the design blueprints when one buys a car! So why
> does access to source code of a product you buy become a fundamental
> right?


It isn't a fundamental right - the company can refuse to disclose the
source code, and I will refuse to buy/use it, just like I refuse to buy Coke
(for different reasons, unrelated to the formula being proprietary).

Likewise, a company can weld the engine compartment shut, and
refuse to disclose anything about the internals of a car, but there
would be very few buyers for that kind of car - I certainly wouldn't
buy such a car.

OTOH, it can supply
a full 1000-page shop/repair manual on a CDROM for a nominal
price, like Mercedes-Benz does for all its cars in the US, and find
repeat buyers flocking back for over a 100 years. It's entirely their
choice whether to keep it closed or open, and it's entirely the
choice of the consumer whether to buy it or not. The history of
engineering/technology shows that customers prefer open products/
standards/technology, and the most successful manufacturers
have adapted to that customer preference.

Over time, the same trend will become apparent in computing as well,
and closed products will fall by the wayside. It's already happened to
a lot of products.

-Siva

Hi Aswin,

After your initial mail, I wrote a Python script to scrape the Hindu's
front page and convert it to RSS 2.0. I wanted to put it on some site,
but decided to check with the folks at the Hindu about the legality of
re-purposing their content for syndication. I haven't  received a
reply till date. Anyway I am attaching the script I wrote - it's a
quick hack, but you should be able to modify it easily, if you know a
bit of Python, and use it to scrape any other site.  It uses
BeautifulSoup and ScrapeNFeed, which you find here:
http://www.crummy.com/software/BeautifulSoup/
http://www.crummy.com/software/ScrapeNFeed/

Congrats to "The Mount Road MahaVishnu" for belatedly moving in the
right direction.

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Fri Sep 23 12:24:37 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Fri Sep 23 13:21:02 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] OT: About cola, pesticides and the Green Revolution
Message-ID: <a8f9901205092223545dd269d5@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/23/05, Ravi Kumar Tenneti <rktenneti@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> It is absolutel true and you know better abt the drugs which have been
> banned in other so called advanced countries but available here. We
> will not be able to know which one is banned and which is not.


You just need to research it a little, using Google. And just FYI, there
are a lot of things which are not banned (tobacco, distilled spirits, guns)
in the West, which can be harmful; and likewise, a fair number of things
that have been banned over the years in various countries which are not
necessarily harmful (typewriters, copying machines in the erstwhile USSR).

The same applies for colored drinks also. The test report by Ms.Sunita
> clearly states that there are pesticides in Indian Drinks which were
> not found in the American drinks.


Yes, obviously - and the same applies to *any* source of ground water
in India, including tap water and milk in India.

Why? Because a lot of groundwater in India is pesticide-contaminated,
whereas the same is not the case in the US. A cow grazing on lands
with pesticide-contaminated groundwater will also produce pesticide-
contaminated milk.

And why is the groundwater so contaminated in India? You can thank the
Green Revolution, and its critical dependence on pesticides, fertilizers
and borewell water for producing sugarcane and other resource-intensive
export crops for that. The run-off from the fields, after they've been
sprayed with pesticides, soaks into the ground and contaminates the
groundwater. Before the Green Revolution, the crops were lower-yielding
varieties, which however did not need pesticides and fertilizers to the
same extent.

But atleast we can stop taking these color water as this is definitely
> and slowly killing us just like cigarettes. But most of the youngsters
> also unfortunately arguing that there is nothing wrong in taking these
> as they feel it signifies the style.
>
> Hope our people take a note of this and stop taking these colored drinks.


I guess they'll also have to stop drinking all ground water as well. Don't
forget milk either.

But you'd do better to campaign for stopping the cultivation of
water-intensive
export-oriented cash crops like Sugarcane. It will also have the beneficial
side-effect of reducing the dependence of Indian agriculture on rapidly
depleting fossil fuels (Natural gas -> Methane -> Ammonia -> Urea ->
Fertilizers).
A 6% drop in production of natural gas at Bombay High last month resulted
in a 50% drop in production of Ammonia in India. Think that over carefully,
especially its implications for the possible cause of the next famine in
India.

-Siva

P.S. It helps to avoid drinking carbonated drinks like Coke as well, but for
reasons unrelated to pesticide contamination.

On Fri, 23 Sep 2005 13:20:33 +0530, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:

>
> "Scientists have found that nicotine really does boost certain

Apparently, it isn't nicotine that poses danger. But rather,
traces of other toxic ingredients like tar, Hydrogen Sulphide,
Carbon Monoxide, Ammonia, Formaldehyde, Acetone, Lead and so on
in the cigarette smoke that causes harm to the lungs in the
long run.

OTOH, traces of all the above mentioned elements and compounds
are found almost everywhere within the city (in the air that
we breathe, in food that we eat, and in water that we drink).

So, cannot comment if cigarette smoking is anymore dangerous
than waiting for a bus at Mount Road bus stand :-)

> with pesticide-contaminated groundwater will also produce pesticide-

> Green Revolution, and its critical dependence on pesticides, fertilizers
> and borewell water for producing sugarcane and other resource-intensive
> export crops for that. The run-off from the fields, after they've been
> sprayed with pesticides, soaks into the ground and contaminates the
> groundwater. Before the Green Revolution, the crops were lower-yielding
> varieties, which however did not need pesticides and fertilizers to the
> same extent.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Sep 23 20:03:38 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Sep 23 20:00:08 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (HOSTNAME)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509231947470.29271-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

RMS (Richard M Stallman) Founder of GNU Projects and Free Software
Foundation (FSF). URL: http://www.stallman.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

hostname -- Show/Set the system's host name.

Summary:

Hostname is the program that is used to either display or set the
*current* host, domain or node name of the system.

Examples:

$ hostname -- Display the FQDN (Fully Qualified Domain Name).

$ hostname -a -- Display the alias name of the host.

$ hostname -d -- Display the name of the DNS domain.

$ hostname -i -- Display the IP address(es) of the host.

$ hostname -s -- Display the short host name (Name appear before 1st 
                 dot)

$ hostname -v -- Be verbose and tell what's going on.

# hostname xyz -- Set the host name as 'xyz'.

Read: man hostname 

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Sat Sep 24 13:27:23 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Sep 24 14:32:45 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: OT: About cola, pesticides and the Green Revolution
In-Reply-To: <5526f5a105092305172f5d1981@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a8f9901205092223545dd269d5@mail.gmail.com>
	<5526f5a105092305172f5d1981@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120509240057199052cd@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/23/05, Ravi Kumar Tenneti <rktenneti@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> Please go thro' the mad cow disease and why it has started also then you
> will understand how thirsty those so called American and British companies
> are ...


I'm one of the earliest posters on Usenet pointing out the link between
regenerative
amplification of prions and the practice of feeding rendered cattle meat to
cattle. Do a
Google search - BTW, Gadjusek figured this out in 1964. There is also a
hypotheses
that the initial trigger for the epidemic came from the export of rendered
cattle parts
from India.

We cannot stop Sugar cane production and other things due to various reasons
> but if they stop using Coke Tins (which are harming the Ozone Layer) the
> World will be much better place to live in. You are saying something which
> is a need based thing here in India


Sugarcane cultivation is not need-based - the primary reason that the
acreage under
Sugarcane cultivation was expanded from 1960 onwards is that it was seen as
an easy
way to obtain export earnings from the sale of refined sugar to the same MNC
cola
companies (Coke, Pepsi) that you're so busy deriding now.

Guess what? - there is no free lunch. The 'virtual water' content in sugar
is enormous -
to manufacture 1 kg of refined sugar requires about 1000 times the quantity
of water
to grow the sugarcane and refining the sugar removes all this water and
dumps it into
the ground as polluted waste molasses, heavily contaminated by pesticide.

The net result of growing sugarcane in AP, TN and Maharashtra is that most
of those
areas which had a water table at zero metres (i.e. at the surface) in 1960,
now have a water
table at -100 metres, i.e. desertification has set in vast areas of these
states. The only
way to continue growing sugarcane in these places is through the use of free
electricity
to operate borewells, and through the use of large dams like the Sardar
Sarovar and
the like.

The only silver lining to this is that the Cola MNCs found an even cheaper
alternative
to Indian sugar in the 80s - High-Fructose Corn Syrup, from corn grown
locally in the
US. The market for refined sugar collapsed soon after, and exports from
India to the US
became uneconomic, thus destroying the Greed-Revolution in Sugarcane in AP,
TN
and Maharashtra.

If there's any moral in this story, it is this: You should fall on your
knees and thank
the MNC Cola companies for finding an alternative to sugar. Without it, most
of
the agricultural belt in Southern India would look even worse than it is now
- a desert.

Anyway, Sugarcane cultivation has already started collapsing on its own in
the last
decade as the freebies (free electricity and water) dried up. India has also
turned into a
net importer of sugar (mainly from Australia) in the process. IMHO, that's
perfect,
because every kg of sugar imported is equivalent to saving over 1000 litres
of fresh
water.

To top it all, they are slowly making us to eat the junk food which will
> increase the obesity (Pizzas etc.,)


Nobody is forcing you to eat junk food. If you don't want it, you don't have
to buy and eat it.

-Siva

> It is a fundamental right because it has controlling function like
> government. Do not treat software like product, think it like
> government. Its role is seen in our life, not just as system
> personnel, as end user also. e.g. from bank-to-diagnosis-to-electing
> prime ministers. Software interfers in our personal life. Have you
> ever seen a car taking you to automatically to a red-light area
> without your consent, but a software browser takes me to a such sites
> without consent. Well that is the power of software - it has
> controlling and governing function. That is why software requires
> some public control.

Software products are released for millions of purposes. Maybe there
is a case for compulsorily open sourcing those that have a bearing on
the public good. But this arguement is not valid to insist that all
s/w be open sourced.

> Coming to your coke analogy, do you know that all food items are
> governed by PFA-Prevention of Food Adulration act, which empowers
> government agencies to check the content and take leagal action in
> case it is not fit for human consumption.

 I do not think the PFA will have Coke's formula with them. Coke
actually left India in the 70s because our government insisted that
the formula be revealed. AFAIK their stand is still the same - only
the govt wilted.

> Can government do this say
> for example examining a closed source software which takes you to
> illegal site? Does any such agency exists?

It is not the govts business - at least not directly. If your browser
takes you to an illegal site use another browser. Market forces will
eleminate faulty browsers.

> Tmorw, if we stop drinking this color water, it is loss to the color
> water Company. But consumer will not get affected in any way.

Likewise in s/w too. If you are not happy with a s/w dont use it. It
is the s/w company that is affected. The consumer can use a different
company's product.

> With-out Blueprint, We can repair our car at road side mechanic shop.
> Bcoz only the blueprint is closed, But engine is open(NOT Sealed). I
> can do reverse engg to find what is going on.
> In Closed Source softwares, the Blueprint (Algorithm) and the Engine
> (Code) both are closed.

My analogy is different. The algorithm is the concept/idea that is
still abstract. It is the source code which is the 'blueprint' -
giving a tangible form to the algorithm. The compiled binary is the
'product' which does what it claims to do.

Physical product companies do not make that big a noise about reverse
engineering because the infrastructure cost of replicating the product
is itself a barrier to competition. Where the barrier is not strong
enough product patents come in. Example, a Ferrari model is not
patented but the suspension subsystem might be patented. So, if
patents are OK in other fields (where there are other barriers to
copying) why is it a bad idea in s/w (where the barrier to copying is
weak - by copying I mean rewriting the code... not pirating)?

If the source code of a s/w is to be given out and also there are to
be no s/w patents, how will a software company ensure that the product
it has just released in the market will earn them enough money to pay
for more research, give the programmers a pay hike (the biggest cost
for a s/w company) and offer better returns to its investors? Will not
another company lift the code make fancy modifications to it (just
enough to fool the courts) and sell it at a much lesser price?

Of course, it can be argued that it benefits the end user by being
less expensive! But then, the govt giving free food, free clothes and
free cash also benefits end users. But does it benefit society?

No ! You still have access to the building blocks of your car, which is

essay on HOW he came up with the idea for the program. The fact that you 
can open up your car and see its engine and what all it's wired to, is the 
equivalent of having source code. If one day your car stops working, you 
don't have to find an authorized dealer to repair it, anyone else can. 
See, the car company is giving up a huge opportunity to make money here.. 
they could've welded the bonnet shut, and forced you to come to them 
everytime the car broke down ... hmm, i wonder how mechanical engineers 
feed their kids.

The car comes with source, .. you can take it apart, replace components - 
many of us don't do it, but some people do. What is more, because its 
"open" i have the option of going to third parties for repair, etc. I 
would not buy any other kind of car.

No, its not about free food. If I pay for software, I get to own it,

> Software products are released for millions of purposes. Maybe there
> is a case for compulsorily open sourcing those that have a bearing on
> the public good. But this arguement is not valid to insist that all
> s/w be open sourced.

what do you suggest? some regulating agency list out 'areas' which it
deems to be for public good and then ensure that there are no patents
or closed source stuff in them? do you seriously think such a thing is
feasible? firstly, i could visualise most of the software on my debian
box to be used by millions of the public, but there are closed source
equivalents existing for them. for that matter, i hope you include the
os in this category of software for public good. secondly, software
are complex creatures and companies can use this to their advantage to
escape the list of areas. what if the company calls an equivalent of
emacs a `psycho-analysis software with a variety of add-ons' because
it has the `doctor' package. seems far-fetched but just an example for
the argument....

> It is not the govts business - at least not directly. If your browser
> takes you to an illegal site use another browser. Market forces will
> eleminate faulty browsers.

> Likewise in s/w too. If you are not happy with a s/w dont use it. It
> is the s/w company that is affected. The consumer can use a different
> company's product.

what if the other browser, or for that matter, all browser companies
decide to do this? seems too unprobable? this is what M$ has been
trying to do all these years. either make opponents agree to their
principles, or buy them out...this idea of using competition to ward
off all evils isn't a good solution, as it assumes the competitors do
not have cooperation amongst themselves.

> If the source code of a s/w is to be given out and also there are to
> be no s/w patents, how will a software company ensure that the product
> it has just released in the market will earn them enough money to pay
> for more research, give the programmers a pay hike (the biggest cost
> for a s/w company) and offer better returns to its investors? Will not
> another company lift the code make fancy modifications to it (just
> enough to fool the courts) and sell it at a much lesser price?

there are ppl who argue that money can be made out of free software. i
think such an argument is hardly necessary. closed source is
*anti-social*. period. it is a non-issue if it causes loss to
companies and programmers who thrive by it. there are many anti-social
activities in real life which can give you loads of dough. i am sure
you don't want me to give examples.

> Of course, it can be argued that it benefits the end user by being
> less expensive! But then, the govt giving free food, free clothes and
> free cash also benefits end users. But does it benefit society?

Mr. RMS, you are the greatest failure I've ever seen. Even after a
decade of crying coarse, people don't seem to realise that fsf exists
not to make things inexpensive, but to give users much needed power.

it moves on...

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sat Sep 24 19:56:32 2005
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Sat Sep 24 19:56:50 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...
In-Reply-To: <7bf1bec50509240206595cc9e3@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7bf1bec505092222091efabc5f@mail.gmail.com>
	<20050923052917.70245.qmail@web8610.mail.in.yahoo.com>
	<7bf1bec50509240206595cc9e3@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <op.sxl2eiawv8spko@xaero.intranet.vetrije.com>

On Sat, 24 Sep 2005 14:36:11 +0530, Mano <manokaran@gmail.com> wrote:

> My analogy is different. The algorithm is the concept/idea that is
> still abstract. It is the source code which is the 'blueprint' -
> giving a tangible form to the algorithm. The compiled binary is the
> 'product' which does what it claims to do.

A 'blueprint' clearly denotes (or rather documents) the idea/design
of a product. In that sense, a documented algorithm could be considered
as the blueprint of the program. The source-code and binary are
mere implementation mechanism.

> If the source code of a s/w is to be given out and also there are to
> be no s/w patents, how will a software company ensure that the product
> it has just released in the market will earn them enough money to pay
> for more research, give the programmers a pay hike (the biggest cost
> for a s/w company) and offer better returns to its investors?

Of course, by following the tunes of Software Freedom/Open Source, you
cannot become the world's richest man in a decade and/or own the world's
most dominant/powerful software company. But... you can definitely
run a company thats profitable, make enough money to pay for more
research and keep your investors happy too. For example, look up
Red Hat Inc., MySQL AB., SleepyCat Software Inc., Sendmail Inc., ...
- the list can go on.

You can either run a company merely for the sake of "making money"
to become rich and famous or for the sake of improving the
standards of life in general (or both). When you support/promote
  Software Freedom/Open Source as the key component of your business
practices, you are clearly trying to portray yourself as an ethical
business entity and also aid in contributing for the betterment
of "free" and "open" society in general. You can definitely make
money either by services/support or even get funded by larger
organizations/government to continue research and development of your
product while remaining a true believer in Free Software/Open Source.

Selling closed source software is as good as selling a car with its
bonnet sealed. Heck, I wouldn't even buy a sealed watch... why even
bother purchasing/trusting a sealed car or closed source software ?!

> Will not another company lift the code make fancy modificationsto it  
> (just enough to fool the courts) and sell it at a much lesserprice?

That could happen in a closed source environment using reverse
engineering techniques. If a company lifts a GPL'ed code for instance
and makes any modifications to it, it is duty-bound to release the
modified source to the public as well which in turn helps the original
author/company to incorporate those changes into their original software
project/product if those changes are useful. Such being the case, now
tell me who wins and who loses ? ;-)

Of course, with a more flexibile license like the BSD license, it is
possible that a company creating a closed source project could lift
the code and merely give a 2 line credit (which to my knowledge, almost
all major closed source OSes do) without having to disclose the modified
source. It all depends on the original author/company on how much of
ownership they want on their code and how aggressive they want to be with
regards to modification/redistribution of their code.

Regarding the cost factor - to my knowledge, most open source products
dont sell at a "fancy" cost. What is mostly sold are service and support
and the cost of service/support is directly dependent on the company's
reputation, their infrastructure/facilities and their expertise/experience.
Just because there are several hundred (or thousand ?) linux distributions
based on Red Hat Linux for the enterprise segment, it doesn't mean that
Red Hat is losing money - do they ? :-)

> Of course, it can be argued that it benefits the end user by being
> less expensive! But then, the govt giving free food, free clothes and
> free cash also benefits end users. But does it benefit society?

It is clearly *not* "free lunch" that we are talking about.
Free Software/Open Source is about "freedom" to use the software
the way we like and to modify/contribute/redistribute them to our
satisfaction.

Information/Technology must remain free (as in freedom) for us to
evolve to better standards of life.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

> Sugarcane cultivation is not need-based - the primary reason that the
> acreage under
> Sugarcane cultivation was expanded from 1960 onwards is that it was seen
> as an easy
> way to obtain export earnings from the sale of refined sugar to the same
> MNC cola
> companies (Coke, Pepsi) that you're so busy deriding now.
>
> Guess what? - there is no free lunch. The 'virtual water' content in sugar
> is enormous -
> to manufacture 1 kg of refined sugar requires about 1000 times the
> quantity of water
> to grow the sugarcane and refining the sugar removes all this water and
> dumps it into
> the ground as polluted waste molasses, heavily contaminated by pesticide.
>
> The net result of growing sugarcane in AP, TN and Maharashtra is that most
> of those
> areas which had a water table at zero metres (i.e. at the surface) in
> 1960, now have a water
> table at -100 metres, i.e. desertification has set in vast areas of these
> states. The only
> way to continue growing sugarcane in these places is through the use of
> free electricity
> to operate borewells, and through the use of large dams like the Sardar
> Sarovar and
> the like.
>
> The only silver lining to this is that the Cola MNCs found an even cheaper
> alternative
> to Indian sugar in the 80s - High-Fructose Corn Syrup, from corn grown
> locally in the
> US. The market for refined sugar collapsed soon after, and exports from
> India to the US
> became uneconomic, thus destroying the Greed-Revolution in Sugarcane in
> AP, TN
> and Maharashtra.
>
> If there's any moral in this story, it is this: You should fall on your
> knees and thank
> the MNC Cola companies for finding an alternative to sugar. Without it,
> most of
> the agricultural belt in Southern India would look even worse than it is
> now - a desert.
>
> Anyway, Sugarcane cultivation has already started collapsing on its own in
> the last
> decade as the freebies (free electricity and water) dried up. India has
> also turned into a
> net importer of sugar (mainly from Australia) in the process. IMHO, that's
> perfect,
> because every kg of sugar imported is equivalent to saving over 1000

> water.

then we need a place to share our non tech issues. As Mr.Toufeeqh rightly
suggest a yahoo group may be place to facilitate our purpose.

I feel the role of ilugc is not just discussing technical issues alone but
also to bring a social change of inculcating foss (like linux) to the
general public. In social mood people tend to discuss variety of subject and
if it is going to be bounded by some rules & regulations in the camp where
we talk about freedom, i would classify that this is the highest degree of
irony to freedom.At the same time i do know the bandwidth issues of ilugc
and using/misusing it has to be handled by the list admin by looking the
issue to its merits.

If issues like drinking coke( i seen this issue in a thread) is been
classified a off-topic issues , we need a place to discuss broader spectrum
of change in the society. Policing on guidelines ruins the freedom instead
providing alternative idea/place/space on server may be appreciated.


Sincerely

Thyagarajan Shanmugham

On 9/24/05, S.Ramaswamy <srsy70@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> While you are in the
> middle of one of these so called revolutions (green, white, etc) there
> is a religious fervour all around and it is very diffcult to have a
> rational discussion. Imagine trying to criticize M.S.Swaminathan or
> C.Subramaniam even today !


You are correct - India does not yet have the capability of critical
Scientific Thought in the Western Tradition. The statistics on the
large numbers of scientists and engineers who graduate every year
are misleading - very few of them would be able to think independently.
We tend to follow the herd in Science and Technology.

The actual impact becomes clear only down
> the road. Right now we are in the middle of another one of these
> hyped-up phases - IT revolution or whatever, that is also massively
> subsidized and is the beneficiary of enormous tax breaks that other
> industries don't enjoy. The impact of this could be lot less physical
> some ways compared with the Sugarcane industry, but be a lot more
> profound in terms of social impact and a lot less intractable.


Touche! The so-called IT revolution is also unsustainable, IMHO; but
it's probably better than the craze for heavy industry that characterized
the Nehruvian era. Let's see how it goes - but I see a tendency to
serfdom as a result of an emphasis on service (to the West, in this
case) rather than ownership/self-determination.

-Siva

on ilugc and most of the non-tech discussions which currently I think some
people just prefer to shift+del can be moved to ilugc-non-tech.

Cross-posting between ilugc and ilugc-non-tech however will not be allowed,
though mails can be directed to ilugc-non-tech if the List Admin feels they
do not belong in ilugc.

just my 2 paise.

Subject: [Ilugc] [OSS Projects] CinePaint call for OSS developers
In-Reply-To: <13ec01c5c1ad$7a195270$0300a8c0@cary>
References: <13ec01c5c1ad$7a195270$0300a8c0@cary>
Message-ID: <99a2c7890509252121786ddf7f@mail.gmail.com>

Hi All,
 CinePaint is a open source deep paint project lead by Robin for a
few years. CinePaint is used on many feature films for dust-busting,
retouching, etc. Currently the team is overhauling CinePaint with a new
architecture called
Glasgow that uses FLTK. Scheduled for release the end of this year. Will
replace legacy code based on Film Gimp and GTK1.

Looking for C++ developers interested in the motion picture industry who'd
like to join the team of a fun open source project.
 Please contact me off-list. I would consolidate and forward the list to
Robin.

Thank you!

Ananth

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Mon Sep 26 14:20:17 2005

On 9/26/05, Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com> wrote:
>
> On Sat, 24 Sep 2005, Mano wrote:
>
> > Likewise in s/w too. If you are not happy with a s/w dont use it. It
> > is the s/w company that is affected. The consumer can use a
> > different company's product.
>
> What will you do with data/files, which are in closed format. Will you
> redo it ??


The main issue in the closed vs. open debate is actually protocols/
data formats. This is still an issue even with FLOSS - although it may
be possible to examine the source to try to understand the protocols/
formats, it is by no means easy or even guaranteed to be possible -
remember that OpenOffice source is now over 100 MBytes.

That's why it's important to have open data formats, and also one
of the reasons that the State of Massachusetts has mandated that
all documents created for/by state agencies will have to be in one
of several open formats, including OpenDocument and PDF. IMHO,
this is a more practical and effective way for the Govt. to push
the use of open standards, than to try to prescribe the specific
software that is meant to be to used.

As long as the document format is open, I'm OK with the consumer
choosing either closed or open-source tools to manipulate it - from
a practical point of view, FLOSS tools will probably win on features
as well as reliability, but it will also allow ISVs to offer closed-source
solutions, *provided* it passes a rigorous test suite (say, it needs
to be able to read/write/print a large set of documents and have them
read/write/print correctly on a reference FLOSS implementation like
Abiword/OpenOffice as well).

-Siva

CALL FOR PROPOSAL
Sarai/CSDS Short Term FLOSS Fellowship, 2005 - 2006.

The Sarai Programme, Centre for the Study of Developing Societies,
Delhi (www.sarai.net) invites applications for fellowship to projects
in the area of Free Software, Open Source Software and Social Usage
of Software.

Sarai invites developers/researchers/ programmers (practitioners as
well as students) to propose projects in the area of free and open
source software applications relevant to educational, social and
community needs.  We are looking for original ideas, as well as
proposals to localize and adapt existing software and applications to
South Asian conditions. We are also looking for ideas around technical
manuscripts,beginners manuals, review manuscripts etc.

Some of the focus areas are:

- Indic Computing
- Developing/Distributing/Supporting a standalone / addon localized
Linux distribution

- Printing support (i.e. ability to print in Indian Languages)

- Multimedia / Publishing Tools Research

- Developing / Enhancing Tools like GIMP, Scribus for publishing
quality work
  - Enhancing current audio/video tools available under Linux

  - Fixing/Supporting Cinelerra, LiVES etc

- P2P

- Researching on feasibility and implementation of P2P news
distribution network

- Researching and developing

- Collaboration Tools/Frameworks
 (Apnaopus, CreativeDot  )

- Developing extensions for the project newsrack(
http://floss.sarai.net/newsrack ).

- Low Resource Computing

- Devising solutions for networked computing in Low Resource Spaces
 (Define the parameters of the "low resource space" and work on it)


- Generic

- Developing Linux drivers/software for easily available hardware
 (usually the cheapest hardware available on the market is not
supported under Linux (scanners, webcams etc))

 [ This would include writing a howto on how to get it to work under
   popular distributions (redhat, pcqlinux etc) and all..    ]

- Review papers on emerging technologies
 - Indic Computing

 - IPV6

 - Wireless Networks

- Manuscripts for beginners


What is Sarai:
_____________

Sarai is a public initiative of media practitioners and scholars
looking at media cultures and urban life. Sarai's interests are in
the field of old  and
new media, information and communication technologies, free software, 
cinema,
and urban space - its politics, built form, ecology, culture and
history, with a strong commitment to making knowledge available in
the public domain.
It is a programme of the Centre for the Study of Developing
Societies, Delhi.

For more information visit www.sarai.net . Sarai is committed to
promoting the
free software and open source vision.

Conditions:
__________
Applicants should be resident in India, and should have a bank
account  in any
bank operating in India.

These are support grants and grantees will be free to pursue their
primary occupations, if any.

Mail your project proposal, workplan and CV to both the following  
addresses:

<floss at sarai.net <https://mail.sarai.net/mailman/listinfo/prc> >

Please mark your subject line 'FLOSS (Free/Libre Open Source
Software) Initiative'.  Also point out what you see as the relevance
of your work, and how you plan to share the resultant software once
finalized.

Enquires: <floss at sarai.net 
<https://mail.sarai.net/mailman/listinfo/prc>>
Last date for submission: November 15th, 2005

Note: Proposals from teams, partnerships, collectives, faculty are
welcome, so long as the grant amount is administered by a single
individual, and the funds are deposited in a single bank account in
the name of an individual.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Sep 26 19:43:09 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Sep 26 19:42:03 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (STRACE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509261923110.4933-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

RMS (Richard M Stallman) Founder of GNU Projects and Free Software
Foundation (FSF). URL: http://www.stallman.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

strace -- Trace System Calls and Signals.

Summary:

In the simplest case strace runs the specified command until it exits.  
It intercepts and records the system calls which are called by a
process and the signals which are received by a process.  The name of
each system call, its arguments and its return value are printed.
strace is a useful diagnostic, instructional, and debugging tool.

Examples:

$ strace sleep 1 -- Trace all Sys call of 'sleep' command.

$ strace ls -- Trace all Sys call of 'ls' command.

$ strace -i sleep 1 -- Print the value of the Instruction Pointer at
                       every sys call.

$ strace -r sleep 1 -- Print a relative time-stamp with each line of
                       the trace.

$ strace -t sleep 1 -- Prefix each line of the trace with the time of
                       day.

$ strace -T sleep 1 -- Show time spent on each call.

$ strace -o file sleep 1 -- Redirect the output to a file.

$ strace -c ls -- Count  time,  calls, and errors for each system call
                   and report a summary on program exit.

$ strace -xx myprg -- Print all strings in HEX format.

$ strace -e trace=file ls -- Trace all system calls which take a
                             filename as an argument. 

$ strace -e trace=process ls -- Trace all system calls which involve
                                process management.

$ sleep 60 & -- Dummy background Job.

$ strace -p 1234 -- Attach to the process with the PID 1234 (use 
                    dummy job's Pid) and trace.

Read: man strace

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

Starting and stopping multi-threaded programs:
http://theory.uwinnipeg.ca/gnu/gdb/gdb_39.html

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Sep 27 19:03:17 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Sep 27 19:01:57 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SYNC)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509271902480.12414-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Eric S. Raymond (ESR), Well known Hacker in FOSS & Unix World, Author
of "The Cathedral and the Bazaar" & "Art of Unix Programming", and 
maintainer of the "Jargon File". URL: http://www.catb.org/~esr/

One Day One Command 
===================

sync -- Flush File System Buffers.

Summary:

The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)  
disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
result.

`sync' used to Synchronize data on disk with memory. 'sync' writes any
data buffered in memory out to disk.

Examples:

$ sync -- Write buffered data to disk.

Read: man sync

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From binand at gmail.com  Tue Sep 27 16:25:06 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Wed Sep 28 01:55:17 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SYNC)
In-Reply-To: <5ef2113c0509271222201ab858@mail.gmail.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509271902480.12414-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
	<5ef2113c0509271222201ab858@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610509271325574dadc8@mail.gmail.com>

On 27/09/05, Senthil Kumaran <stylesen@gmail.com> wrote:
> I have a doubt.. why there is a need for sync.. why the data is not
> witten to the memory as soon as it is reffered to.. is it important to
> have this delay...

Bharti's summary explains it:

"The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)
disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
result."

The kernel automatically flushes these in-core buffers as and when
they become full; the sync(8) command (and the sync(2) system call) is
for forcing this flush operation.

Binand

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Wed Sep 28 10:13:22 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Wed Sep 28 10:13:00 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] NISG NeGP initiative at a cost of Rs.14,000 CRORES
Message-ID: <433A1F6A.70600@gmail.com>

National Institute for Smart Government (NISG) is driving the National 
e-Governance Plan (NeGP) and estimated to cost Rs. 14,000 Crores.

Governance has evolved by trial and error over a very long period of 
time, much the way free software evolves these days. Governance was 
thought best to be divided into legislative, executive and judiciary. 
eGovernance could avoid the many prejudices a human executive suffers, 
and the old divisions have to be redefined. Compare:

developer : user :: legislator : citizen

A BDFL manages the developer:user gap pretty much, and the right to fork 
satisfies the disgruntled in the unlimited virtual world. The 
legislator:citizen relationship is constrained severlely by limited 
resources, and there could be no right to fork. It is for this reason, 
the Constitutional machinery elaborately defines how citizens govern 
themselves by electing legislators. The existing Constitutional 
machinery assumes paper as the medium through which the laws will be 
executed. Writ of certiorari traditionally meant "calling for the 
(physical) records" - now, if a judge could "visit" the files through an 
electronic medium, the scope, nature and methods of the writ stands 
vastly modified. Each and every constitutional device, control and 
measure has to be modified to suit the new medium of execution. 
Traditionally, constitutions are classified as written and unwritten, 
and today we have to create a new classification electronic and 
non-electronic. The constitutional machinery has to be totally rebuilt 
from scratch to suit the new medium. eGovernance actually calls for 
serious debates on constitutional reform before spending a single rupee 
on any eGovernance program.

Sprinkling "IBM", "Linux", "Open Source", "Open Standards" and other 
catch words here and there over the project are mere incidental things 
that do not go to the core issues of governance. Does the GOI expect IBM 
to give the framework for eGovernance? Is Indian legislative history 
(1600 - 1950) repeating itself ? E-Courts has been added to their 
planning boards as an after thought, and clearly shows poor planning. 
Burning 14K Crores (in two years ?) over NeGP, that too controlled by 
NASSCOM sounds very stupid, to say the least. They are looking for 
consultants (apply at your own risk ;) and I hope they don't get too 
smart ;) Bullock carts fitted with electric motors won't move 
efficiently - NiSG is only doing this and this is not my imagination: 
their advt calling for consultants has the wheel of a bullock cart with 
an e in the centre :)

There are other strange issues there too:

As a last resort you can boot your system with a windows boot disk,
and in C: type "fdisk /mbr".
This will restore the MBR in your active partition and you can boot
into windows.
Booting into Linux won't be possible because this command  overwrites grub.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Wed Sep 28 10:33:15 2005
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy)
Date: Wed Sep 28 10:31:08 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (SYNC)
In-Reply-To: <d2a92d610509271325574dadc8@mail.gmail.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509271902480.12414-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>	<5ef2113c0509271222201ab858@mail.gmail.com>
	<d2a92d610509271325574dadc8@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <433A2413.9090105@tandbintl.com>

   For example, if you are using a old hard disk with latest processor
   system, the seek time of hdd will be more which will be lagging behind the
   processor speed. When the logs are written in a file in hdd, you may not
   able to see the appending of data in a log file immediately through 'tail
   -f logfile' command. just a 'sync' will set right it. I found this command
   useful in sco-unix systems.

   Regards
   T.KaruppuSwamy

   Binand Sethumadhavan wrote:

 On 27/09/05, Senthil Kumaran <stylesen@gmail.com> wrote:
  

 I have a doubt.. why there is a need for sync.. why the data is not
 witten to the memory as soon as it is reffered to.. is it important to
 have this delay...
    

 Bharti's summary explains it:

 "The Linux Kernel keeps data in memory to avoid doing (relatively slow)
 disk reads and writes.  This improves performance, but if the computer
 crashes, data in memory may be lost or the file system corrupted as a
 result."

 The kernel automatically flushes these in-core buffers as and when
 they become full; the sync(8) command (and the sync(2) system call) is
 for forcing this flush operation.

 Binand

> Please correct me if I am wrong.

Hello all -

Let me first explain you the reason behind starting this group. As far 
as Hurd is concerned, there are only limited set of support resources 
available on the web. But most of these resources are outdated. When a 
new user who would like to try out Hurd, I think that he feels a bit 
lost even after googling enough. People can subscribe to help-hurd 
mailing list. But it has a very low (really low) signal to noise ratio. 
A lot of spams posted everyday. I have observed that people from our 
group like Shakthi Kannan, Joe Steeve, Anand Babu are doing a good work 
having a good amount of knowledge on Hurd. If we can get them join in 
one place to provide valuable help for Hurd users, it would be great.

It is true that most of the Hurd users are Linux users but not even a 
considerable amount of Linux users are Hurd users. I don't think all 
Linux users in the UG will welcome Hurd discussions. At some point in 
time or the other, flame wars may rise. As the number of Hurd users are 
very less at this point in time, it would not be ideal to have a region 
specific UG in India. So, we thought it would be better to have a nation 
wide UG instead of having it region specific like Bangalore, Chennai or 
Delhi. Now in our group, we have users from Chennai, Bangalore, Delhi, 
Goa, etc. With this diversity of users, it is known fact that we can't 
meet physically as the typical LUG meeting. Instead, the meeting would 
be on IRC similar to the traditional meeting of any free software 
developers community.

Please do correct us if our stand is wrong in this aspect.

Thanks -
Praveen.

-- 
Praveen Kumar
http://www.praveen.ws

From simplesupply at yahoo.com  Wed Sep 28 02:13:23 2005
From: simplesupply at yahoo.com (Venky)
Date: Wed Sep 28 14:43:32 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Windows 2000/XP grub problem
Message-ID: <20050928091323.12204.qmail@web32410.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

As Sujith said it seems that the MBR file has been overwritten. 
Using a windows boot disk you can fix the mbr by giving the following command:
      c:\>fdisk /mbr
This will fix your windows booting problem. But you will not be able to boot into linux anymore as the mbr is again over written with the 'fdisk /mbr' command.
 
To recover linux boot:
I have got a way which I have published in my blog:
 
Please visit: http://geekollection.blogspot.com/2005/04/get-back-dual-boot-linux-windows.html
 
I hope this will help you recover the dual boot.
 
regards
Venkatesh.

Yahoo! for Good
 Click here to donate to the Hurricane Katrina relief effort.

First: Don't top post.

Second: Why re-invent the wheel ?
There is a perfectly good initiative called IndLinux
http://indlinux.orgwhich is heavily into
localization.Why don't you and your friends join up with them and better
that distro rather than start afresh ?

Anyway, I always thought installing debian using the basedebs.tar.gz package
as a form of customized distro,ofcourse you don't compile packages(but
install binaries,deb's) but starting off with a minimal Debian distro gives
you the same freedom which you can find in a LFS based one.

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Wed Sep 28 16:29:27 2005
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R)
Date: Wed Sep 28 16:29:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Problem with Microphone
In-Reply-To: <f190c8a505092622431f854db4@mail.gmail.com>
References: <f190c8a505092622431f854db4@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc1705092803597ecc69a1@mail.gmail.com>

> managed to record anything. I've tried KRec, Gnome Sound Recorder and
> Audacity. The recording input widget in KDE doesn't show any input

hey aparajit, have u ensured that the software you're using have been
configured to use alsa? perhaps they are by default trying to use oss,
esound or something like that. may be u can provide the output of
/proc/asound/cardN/pcmNc/subN/status (N is usually 0), while you try
to record. It should say RUNNING. In case the app supports OSS, may be
u can try the OSS emulation of ALSA (u will need to modprobe
snd-pcm-oss and snd-mixer-oss) or try running the program with aoss.
That will perhaps help us decide if it is indeed a configuration
problem.

connect to internet without making configuration in your software
irrespective of the OS.

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Wed Sep 28 20:58:16 2005
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R)

Subject: [Ilugc] custom distro

Message-ID: <9a9bfc17050928082860118584@mail.gmail.com>

>  there are various reasons for building a customized distribution.We are
> having many ideas like improving the GUI,Fonts,Localization,Updation and
> some new ideas.Yes,ofcourse there are linux distributions which are really
> good and reliable..but why dont we try?...thats when u can feel the real
> "Free"dom!

I appreciate your enthusiasm for creating a new distro from scratch,
but like others have said, it would be great if you could consider
incorporating your ideas to some existing distro, unless you really
feel that *all* existing distro are not fundamentally suited for your
improvements. Distros like debian, gentoo have excellent systems in
place which allow enormous customization, and will most probably have
mechanisms to include your ideas. Even if they don't, I'm sure they
will love patches which help making their framework much more flexible
and accomodating. Having said all this, if your motive is purely
educational, a new distro is a great idea, but please ensure that you
either merge your ideas into some existing distro or atleast list them
down in some distro wishlist, so that other ppl could probably take it
up...

it moves on....
