From trshash84 at gmail.com  Wed Sep 28 21:35:17 2005
From: trshash84 at gmail.com (T.R.Shashwath)
Date: Wed Sep 28 21:34:26 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Buying a modem for BSNL DATAONE
In-Reply-To: <4dc6c904050928062434bac558@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e0900f3e0509280423770d8b8a@mail.gmail.com>
	<4dc6c904050928062434bac558@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200509282135.17914.trshash84@gmail.com>

On Wednesday 28 September 2005 18:54, Bhuvaneswaran A wrote:
> On 9/28/05, Rajagopal Natarajan <rajagopal.n@gmail.com> wrote:
> > What company (and what model no) ADSL USB modem should I buy for BSNL
> > DATAONE, so that I can configure it in linux?
>
> You can get from BSNL itself. The modems provided by them are
> compatible with GNU/Linux. For me they have given UTSTAR ADSL MODEM
> (ethernet). It's doing great. BTW,  similar modem should be available
> in ritche street as well. On the other hadn, on configuration front,
> you can set the userid/password in the modem. It would enable you to
> connect to internet without making configuration in your software
> irrespective of the OS.

In general, any ethernet modem (that works with PPPoE) will be fine with 
Rp-PPPoE. That is to say, any ethernet modems will work. If they insist on 
giving you an idiotic USB modem (and ONLY as a last option), try to get a 
Globespan based one, since we have a usermode driver for that.

Finally, if you're using multiple systems, it makes more sense to have a DSL 
router and a hub or a switch. Sure, it costs (much) more, but it's worth it. 
You can get a DLink router here in India, which is quite good...

Just be sure you get all (and I mean ALL) the configuration details from the 
BSNL guys - VPI/VCI, login and password.

-- 
Shash

reasons...

keeping in mind the BSNL modem, so even if you try configuring them your
self, you may find difficulty in corelating things, as all modem's
interfaces are all not alike, (infact, even same company models have
different interfaces for configuring.)
3. The modem BSNL provides is good in cost and features etc .. unless
you are thinking to go for a wireless or other featured modems.
Configuring the modems to work is really an easy task, you need to do
hit and trail methods untill you find the right settings. ( At least
this happend for me , for my DLINK Modem)

In-Reply-To: <433B6C97.80009@tandbintl.com>
References: <e0900f3e0509280423770d8b8a@mail.gmail.com>
	<4dc6c904050928062434bac558@mail.gmail.com>
	<200509282135.17914.trshash84@gmail.com>

Message-ID: <a8f9901205092822252423c7d5@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/29/05, T.KaruppuSwamy <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:

>
> Why do you call USB Modem as **idiotic** ? Can any one brief me the
> technical aspect of it?
>

Several reasons:

1) The functional partitioning is not clean - there need to be several
layers
inside the USB Modem (USB client-side stack, PPPoA emulation, ADSL
end-point stack, ...). There has to also be a functional Linux host driver
that
can talk to such a complex device, that will work with a wide variety of USB
host-side chipsets and drivers (OHCI, UHCI, EHCI, ...).

The odds of this happening are low - the far-eastern manufacturers tend
to have poor records in implementing Linux drivers themselves, and they
rarely release good documentation for their product implementations.

2) USB is host-side CPU resource hog - it tends to use interrupts for just
about anything, soaking up a lot of CPU cycles on ISRs, context-switches
and cache/TLB flushes. The reasons for this are historical - Intel wanted
to sell faster and faster PII/PIII CPUs, and the best way to convince users
to upgrade was to use up CPU cycles on USB.

You'll be better off without a single connected USB device on your
system. If you ever need to use it all, use it sparingly, for instance
to download images from a Digicam.

3) The alternative is to use an Ethernet-connected ADSL modem.
These are cleaner/simpler implementations, using PPPoE or vanilla
TCP/IP over Ethernet. The odds of getting all the stacks working
well are far better.

-Siva

 first i would like to thank everyone in this group for your replies.I was
really happy to see the replies.Since i could reply for every mail, am
starting another theread..
 Many had given me new ideas.Well, the reason why we chose to go from
scratch and not taking an existing distro is, -

Suppose u find something has to be tweaked or optimized in the existing
distro,anyhow u have to re-compile the package (or) if u find some problem
with that version used u have to install the proper version.Now what happens
is, we would not know whether removal of that particular package will affect
the system or not.This will become very critical.

Suppose at the same time if u have proper documentation on each and every
package provided by the system, then it would be good to proceed with the
existing distro.

The idea of promoting Linux at Schools is an excellent start.Anyway we need
all the optimizations and tweakings done.If proper documentation is there
for the freeduc edition in the packages list and the base-system, it would
be gud to proceed.Otherwise, it will be very tough.People who can help me
with freeduc can approach me.I tried the link http://ofset.org/freeducgiven,
but it didnt work.

Creating LiveCDS will help us in the initial stages, but once people get
used to our distro, it is good to have an installable system.LiveCDS can be
used for just Demo and learning purpose.

I have good experience in LFS and we also have LFS plan put up.But that is a
long way.....we integrated RPM with LFS and had a base system with PM in a
stand alone system but it was difficult for us to create a base system
installer.We have to plan for such a environment.

Am also working with YOPER and i have seen their's Base System
Development.It closely resembles LFS.How YOPER is the fastest OS ?..its
because of the optimizations they have used in their kernel and in other
packages.

We are also trying to get a base system, and build from there.But until now
we havent thought of any good base system.I think we will be trying with the
Debian Base System...any ideas in this?..whatever the case, base system
should be stable,reliable and updatable...

hope i made clear a little bit..

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Sep 29 00:55:12 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Sep 29 13:25:31 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Buying a modem for BSNL DATAONE
In-Reply-To: <433B6C97.80009@tandbintl.com>
Message-ID: <20050929075512.42006.qmail@web50208.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

My thoughts below:

--- "T.KaruppuSwamy" <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
> Why do you call USB Modem as **idiotic** ? Can any
> one brief me the 
> technical aspect of it?

1. Although USB high-speed (HS) is 480 Mbps compared
to ethernet 100 Mbps, most USB devices can only behave
as "devices" that can be connected to a computer or
USB hub. Only now you will find USB OTG products in
the market, US and Taiwan.

2. Its easier and cheaper to setup a LAN with ethernet
than USB.

3. Most ISPs provide USB modems so that you can only
use one computer with the Internet. If you want to use
it with another computer, they will ask you to buy
another connection? This is what Touchtel told me.
There was one ISP marketing guy who told me it was
illegal to share bandwidth from the ISP connection.
Huh! I referred him to RFC 1631 for doing NAT (at
home):

http://www.faqs.org/rfcs/rfc1631.html

4. USB was primarily designed for embedded than for
large networks.

5. Most USB modems are like winmodems, with vendors
not providing much details on their chipsets.

HTH,

SK

I use touchtel, no problems with sharing connectivity. :)
Just show the sales guy a Linux login and tell him that you use Linux/UNIX.
He'll just panic and say "USB modems may not run,Sir".

Insist on a Ethernet based Modem,remember the word "ethernet" keep saying
that otherwise he'll just get you a USB one.It also "behaves" as a router
with NAT,DHCP etc.

When the install guy gets the router/modem, get him to setup the h/w and
then just open firefox and point it to the ethernet modem(something like
192.168.1.1 <http://192.168.1.1>).He'll take care of the rest.

Assign an IP to your PC (192.168.1.3 <http://192.168.1.3>) and you are good
to go.

Use the modem/router's IP as your gateway.

-toufeeq

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Thu Sep 29 15:34:05 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 29 15:34:27 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] For discussion: Linux misses Windows of opportunity
In-Reply-To: <433BA9C2.203@tandbintl.com>
References: <433BA9C2.203@tandbintl.com>
Message-ID: <a8f99012050929030414dc6082@mail.gmail.com>

On 9/29/05, T.KaruppuSwamy <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
>
>
> The following article describes the issue faced by a SAP implementation
> on Linux. Though it is not elaborated more technically, let us have a
> discussion on it.
>
>
> http://www.theage.com.au/articles/2005/09/26/1127586780339.html?from=top5&oneclick=true


The problems were specific to their deployment of SAP on RedHat, and their
inability to hire a competent IT team to deploy it. There are any number of
unsuccessful/delayed/bloated deployments of SAP on any platform, so this
is not surprising. BTW, SAP is not very well regarded for their Linux
support -
that may change eventually.

Those idiots actually wanted to automate their application of updates (they
call it "auto-patch" - M$ terminology). It's fairly easy with RHN and/or
yum,
but why would anybody do that in a production environment? There are no
serious holes in a typical RHEL install, so I'd simply let it run in peace
and
manually update selective RPMs based on RedHat update notifications, say
once a month, unless there is a major security update. There's never any
need to keep updating stuff on a Linux distro all the time - that's only
common
in the M$ world ("Patch Tuesday"), but that's the culture these guys come
from, so it's no surprise that their deployment failed.

-Siva

P.S. "Patching" means very different things in the Unix/Linux and M$ worlds
- one never patches a Linux binary, you only update a package or bunch of
packages. You only patch source code in the Linux world, never a binary
on a production server.

From shirolsh at india.hp.com  Thu Sep 29 18:55:33 2005
From: shirolsh at india.hp.com (Kiran S Shirol)
Date: Thu Sep 29 18:56:50 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] outlook express to evaluation mail
In-Reply-To: <20050929131201.33467.qmail@web32801.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

Message-ID: <1128000333.5743.17.camel@nt217167.india.hp.com>

I am not sure about whether u have a email client  called Evaluation.

Well if you are taking about Evolution then the following is the
solution:

The outlook express uses the .dbx format.
Evolution uses the .mbx format.

Convert all the .dbx files to .mbx format using the following freely 
available tool
     http://people.freenet.de/ukrebs/dbxconv.html

Its called the dbxconv.exe

Once you are done with the conversion,copy these to your linux
partition.

>From the menu of evolution import all the .mbx files.

And Bingo ...... You have your old mail form Outlook express in
Evolution

    ++ Kiran ++

Dear sudharsan.

here is the solution to calculate the transfer
through the network card eth0 or ppp0.

open any console
login as root
type ifconfig
it will give the network details.

for example, here is my output of ifconfig.
I have one Lan card as etho.
lo is loop back.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
eth0      Link encap:Ethernet  HWaddr 00:00:21:EF:9D:DB
          inet addr:192.9.204.214  Bcast:192.9.204.255  Mask:255.255.255.0
          UP BROADCAST RUNNING MULTICAST  MTU:1500  Metric:1
          RX packets:4262355 errors:0 dropped:0 overruns:0 frame:0
          TX packets:28899 errors:0 dropped:0 overruns:0 carrier:0
          collisions:5745
>         RX bytes:281297694 (268.2 Mb)  TX bytes:5515392 (5.2 Mb)

lo        Link encap:Local Loopback
          inet addr:127.0.0.1  Mask:255.0.0.0
          UP LOOPBACK RUNNING  MTU:16436  Metric:1
          RX packets:83664 errors:0 dropped:0 overruns:0 frame:0
          TX packets:83664 errors:0 dropped:0 overruns:0 carrier:0
          collisions:0
          RX bytes:4324366 (4.1 Mb)  TX bytes:4324366 (4.1 Mb)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

note the line denoted as ">" by me.
RX=received  TX=transmitted
it is the amount from system boot.
I have received 268.2MB data from by system boot., through lan.
my system uptime is 11 hrs.

so, for you, i hope ifconfig will show ppp0
after connecting to net, watch ifconfig.
while finishing surfing, watch it and note it down before disconnecting.

try it out and send the results.
i hope it will work for u and satisfy ur need.
if it is not worthy, tell me.
i will search any tool or try to write any script.

ok?

bye n wishes.

dear,
T.Shrinivasan.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Sep 29 20:36:13 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Sep 29 20:34:09 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (LSOF)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509292035510.3557-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Edsger Wybe Dijkstra (EWD) was one of the most influential members of
computing science's founding generation and he honored by ACM Turing 
Award. URL: http://www.cs.utexas.edu/users/EWD/

One Day One Command 
===================

lsof -- LiSt Open Files.

Summary:

lsof lists all open files belonging to all active processes. An open
file may be a regular file, a Dir, a special file, an executing text
reference, a library, a stream or a network file (Internet socket, NFS
file or UNIX domain socket).

Examples:

$ lsof -- List all open files.

$ lsof -i -- List all open Internet files.

$ lsof -U -- List all open Unix Domain files.

$ lsof -u user1 -- List all files opened by User1.

$ lsof -p 1234 -- List all files opened by process with PID of 1234.

$ lsof /dev/hda2 -- List all open files on device /dev/hda2.

$ lsof -s -- List all open files with size.

$ lsof -r 5 -- Repeat the command for every 5 Sec.

Read: man lsof (More examples are available)

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From firaz_ap at rediffmail.com  Thu Sep 29 17:21:49 2005
From: firaz_ap at rediffmail.com (firaz peer)
Date: Thu Sep 29 22:51:50 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Buying a modem for BSNL DATAONE
Message-ID: <20050929172156.20748.qmail@webmail10.rediffmail.com>

  
  



> > 1) The functional partitioning is not clean - there need to be several
> > layers
> > inside the USB Modem (USB client-side stack, PPPoA emulation, ADSL
> > end-point stack, ...). There has to also be a functional Linux host driver
> > that
> > can talk to such a complex device, that will work with a wide variety of USB
> > host-side chipsets and drivers (OHCI, UHCI, EHCI, ...).
> >
> > The odds of this happening are low - the far-eastern manufacturers tend
> > to have poor records in implementing Linux drivers themselves, and they
> > rarely release good documentation for their product implementations.
> >
> > 2) USB is host-side CPU resource hog - it tends to use interrupts for just
> > about anything, soaking up a lot of CPU cycles on ISRs, context-switches
> > and cache/TLB flushes. The reasons for this are historical - Intel wanted
> > to sell faster and faster PII/PIII CPUs, and the best way to convince users
> > to upgrade was to use up CPU cycles on USB.
> >
> > You'll be better off without a single connected USB device on your
> > system. If you ever need to use it all, use it sparingly, for instance
> > to download images from a Digicam.


Hi, i was wonderin if what u have mentioned above is 
restricted to only BSNL USB Modems or is it the case
with all USB Modems? So will i be better off takin
an ethernet one instead of a USB one? Also, is there
any way of connecting to the internet from more than 
one system (simultaneoulsy) while using a USB modem??

In-Reply-To: <20050929172156.20748.qmail@webmail10.rediffmail.com>

On Thursday 29 September 2005 22:51, firaz peer wrote:
> > > 1) The functional partitioning is not clean - there need to be several
> > > layers
> > > inside the USB Modem (USB client-side stack, PPPoA emulation, ADSL
> > > end-point stack, ...). There has to also be a functional Linux host
> > > driver that
> > > can talk to such a complex device, that will work with a wide variety
> > > of USB host-side chipsets and drivers (OHCI, UHCI, EHCI, ...).
> > >
> > > The odds of this happening are low - the far-eastern manufacturers tend
> > > to have poor records in implementing Linux drivers themselves, and they
> > > rarely release good documentation for their product implementations.
> > >
> > > 2) USB is host-side CPU resource hog - it tends to use interrupts for
> > > just about anything, soaking up a lot of CPU cycles on ISRs,
> > > context-switches and cache/TLB flushes. The reasons for this are
> > > historical - Intel wanted to sell faster and faster PII/PIII CPUs, and
> > > the best way to convince users to upgrade was to use up CPU cycles on
> > > USB.
> > >
> > > You'll be better off without a single connected USB device on your
> > > system. If you ever need to use it all, use it sparingly, for instance
> > > to download images from a Digicam.
>
> Hi, i was wonderin if what u have mentioned above is
> restricted to only BSNL USB Modems or is it the case
> with all USB Modems? So will i be better off takin
> an ethernet one instead of a USB one? Also, is there
> any way of connecting to the internet from more than
> one system (simultaneoulsy) while using a USB modem??

Every single USB modem made - BSNL doesn't use anything special... Get the 
ethernet modem!

To answer your second question, I used to do that with a Globespan modem, 
running a NAT server on one system and having everyone connect to that as the 
primary gateway. Unfortunately, it requires the NAT to be online all the 
time. But otherwise, it's decent.

-- 
Shash

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Fri Sep 30 09:09:44 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)

Subject: [Ilugc] Buying a modem for BSNL DATAONE
In-Reply-To: <20050929172156.20748.qmail@webmail10.rediffmail.com>
References: <20050929172156.20748.qmail@webmail10.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120509292039u5d8eb576h32bb11a04216780f@mail.gmail.com>

On 29 Sep 2005 17:21:56 -0000, firaz peer <firaz_ap@rediffmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> Hi, i was wonderin if what u have mentioned above is
> restricted to only BSNL USB Modems or is it the case
> with all USB Modems?


All USB modems - Dial-up, ISDN, DSL, Cable ...

So will i be better off takin
> an ethernet one instead of a USB one?


Yes, it's more likely that ethernet-connected modems will work
out of the box.

Also, is there
> any way of connecting to the internet from more than
> one system (simultaneoulsy) while using a USB modem??


Yes, the machine which connects to the net using the USB
modem should be made into a NAT gateway, and all the
other machines connect to this gateway using Ethernet.

Even this becomes easier if you use an ethernet-connected
modem - there are existing router-centric distros (like Routerlinux)
that will work out of the box with just about any ethernet-connected
modem, and turn the machine into an extremely reliable and secure
NAT/router/firewall box that can easily replace a few $30k Cisco
boxes.

-Siva

Subject: [Ilugc] to provoke thought... not emotion...

References: <7bf1bec505092721295fab5c7f@mail.gmail.com>
	<20050928050118.51144.qmail@web8608.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <7bf1bec50509292232p6097e69o7e6788b73bfe72f9@mail.gmail.com>

This thread has dragged on for too long for everyone's comfort! My
initial question is still unanswered. Maybe because there is no answer
for it yet! But I found this a stimulating exchange. Helped clarify
some points and raised more questions (which is not bad actually). Of
course there were acrimonious posts (aggravated further by me).
Apologies to all aggravated parties :-)

I find it difficult to base my inferences on dogmas (source code is a
fundamental right, businesses are bad etc). I think it will clarify
our thoughts and reinforce our sense of purpose if we periodically
question the very dogmas. But at some level I think one has to have
faith in something to base all his inferences on. I, conveniently base
mine on the kural:

Epporul yaar yaar vai ketpinum
Apporul meiporul kaanbatharivu

(roughly translated it means, 'whatever is said by whoever,
intelligence is to question it till you reach the truth'   purists pls
pardon me) A pretty recursive dogma :-) Questions every creed, every
faith.

The somewhat hazy conclusion I have come to now is that open source
and closed source software will co-exist till it is emphatically
proven that closed source is evil.

As for the last posters accusation about my business bias: I tried my
best to avoid all biases from my arguements. Apologize if some creeped
in. But then, businesses are not evil. They serve an important purpose
in society. Am sure a discussion on this will surely be deemed OT. So
if you are willing, post to ilugc non tech mailing list your vision of
a society driven by purely non profit organizations :-)

There are many more thoughts to provoke.....

regds,
mano

--
Artificial intelligence is no match for natural stupidity.

If India wins - Our Corrupt will loose!!
If India wins - The Rich will loose!!

From: Shiva Shankar <sshankar@cmi.ac.in>

Dear Friends,
        As you know, Dalits affected by the Tsunami have been left out in
the cold, with neither the state government nor NGOs willing to provide
even elementary relief.
        The Sakya Foundation (a grouping of Ambedkarite Buddhists) has
therefore stepped in to provide some succour. We have rented a house at
Manali (New Town) to accomodate children from Nagapattinam and Cuddalore
who have lost parents in the Tsunami (the Sakya Foundation does not
discriminate - the children are from various "communities" - Dalit,
Meenavar (fisherfolk), Muslim etc). These children, at present 60 in
number, are looked after and sent to a local corporation school.
        Impressed by this effort, Professor A.Uma of the Humanities Dept.
of the Central University at Hyderabad has donated a computer (together
with printer etc). We need some person who will check out the computer,
install more software that the children can use and also teach a few
senior children some basics. This will take four or five sessions I
expect.
        I go every Saturday to Manali New Town to teach the children
mathematics. If some person is willing to help with the computer, I can
take the person along with me.
        In anticipation of some help I offer my heartfelt thanks.
                                        Shiva Shankar,
                                        Chennai Mathematical Institute.

On Fri, 2005-09-30 at 11:02, Mano wrote:
> This thread has dragged on for too long for everyone's comfort! My
> initial question is still unanswered. Maybe because there is no answer

> Will OSS be able to deliver an app that defines and creates its own
> market - something like what Photoshop or Dreamweaver or Lotus Notes
> did in their respective domains? Will OSS be able to deliver that tool
> that will mark a paradigm shift in the way people use their computers?

Innovations have been there., it depends on what you consider as an
innovation. Though the Linux kernel is based on UNIX ideas., the
implementation of it has a number of innovations which UNIX did not
have. Loadable kernel modules, Anticipatory I/O scheduling, etc.. The
entire design of the gnu/hurd is a innovation.

Now., these innovations may not be obvious to a business person who
does not know the details of OS technology. A business person., or a
end user merely terms `innovation` as what he can see. However, it is
not so. All technical innovations need not be pleasing or acceptable to
a business person., and vice versa. Now., that is the reason why many
people on this thread where particular on the angle in which you were
approaching the topic, based on your domain/expertise.

Each expert in his area of skill (webservers/ databases/etc..), would
be able to list innovations like these. It depends on what you
acknowledge as a innovation.

-- 
.o. A proud GNU user

ooo http://www.joesteeve.org/

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Fri Sep 30 12:44:30 2005
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy)
Date: Fri Sep 30 12:42:26 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] X window
In-Reply-To: <20050930070519.56288.qmail@web54105.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20050930070519.56288.qmail@web54105.mail.yahoo.com>

You have to add the list of hosts allowed to access other X Server. This 
can be done with xhost command as shown below:
# xhost +<your local host name>
This should  be run at other X Server.

> accidentally enabled the LDAP authentication.(I just
> enabled the checkbox )
>
> I restarted the system and tried to login .Even if i
> give the correct root password it says "Authentication
> Failed".
>

Go into rescue mode using original media, mount root filesystem,
chroot there, mount other filesystems and run authconfig (or
system-config-authentication or redhat-config-authentication - not
sure which one for RH9) again.

hi,


> Go into rescue mode using original media, mount root filesystem,
> chroot there, mount other filesystems and run authconfig (or
> system-config-authentication or redhat-config-authentication - not
> sure which one for RH9) again.

no need to do all that.

u can go to single user mode by passing init parameter to the grub,
which can be done by getting into the edit mode ( use 'e')

then select the kernel line and append it with 1( for single user mode)

once the system has booted up, open the file

/etc/nsswitch.conf
and change or remove the order correspong to users and passwd.
or add entries for loacl accounts,


hope this helped.

regards,
kiran

Also one of my relatives is using a DLINK DSL502T (~Rs. 2k) ADSL
modem. It has one ethernet, one ADSL and one USB interfaces and it
works fine with the BSNL DataOne connection. Connect it to the
ethernet and it works good. As far as the USB interface is concerned
drivers are provided for Windows.

Also this box runs linux. You can telnet to the machine and busybox pops up.
Configuring the box is thro' the http interface and its simple. Also
incase of difficulties i guess the BSNL guys will help in configuring
it.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Sep 30 20:28:31 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Sep 30 20:26:24 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (HDPARM)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0509302027400.11199-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Richard W Stevens author of UNIX Networking Programming and 
TCP/IP Illustrated Book series. URL: http://www.kohala.com/

One Day One Command 
===================

hdparm -- Get/Set Hard Disk Parameters.

Summary:

hdparm provides a command line interface to various hard disk ioctls
supported by the stock Linux ATA/IDE device driver subsystem.

You *MUST* read the man page completely, if you want to do anything
else, apart from this examples.

Examples:

$ hdparm -i /dev/hda -- Display the identification info that was
                        obtained from the drive at boot time.

$ hdparm -I /dev/hda -- Request identification info directly from the
                        drive and display in a new expanded format.

Read: man hdparm

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

Message-ID: <f190c8a50509300201t7ea30f21s4ac8356187951395@mail.gmail.com>

I believe the open source exponent should not try to achieve
conversion by grandstanding, or moralizing or appealing to the 'good
nature' of people. If its being for the good of humanity was reason
enough for people to adopt it, we would have far fewer problems in the
world. Rather, compelling and persuading the non-believer, and not
giving in to throwing one's arms up, is probably the way to go.
Undoubtedly the OSS movement has produced many fantastic innovations,
its a given considering the brilliant and focused brains behind the
project. Explaining this with a pinch of patience does not detract
from the idea.
And making money or business is not evil (yet :). Most of us need our
salaries, I guess. I don't think the world as a whole has evolved
enough to base decisions on altruism, the bottom line continues to
drive the world, and that might not necessarily be a bad thing.
Just my thoughts,
Aparajit
